# Roguelite Design Analysis

## Summary

Extended game design session that evolved from Emoji Ball Battles brainstorming into a comprehensive roguelite taxonomy framework and blog post.

**Emoji Ball Battles Design Doc:**
- Added Earclacks as inspiration for "Weapon Ball" physics format
- Stripped all minesweeper/exploration content, keeping only physics ball combat core (729 → 157 lines)

**Roguelite Taxonomy Framework:**
- Developed 17-axis framework across 6 categories (Acquisition, Management, Information, Progression, Meta, Experience)
- Added 2 subtables: Pacing (under Choice Timing), Commitment Weight (under Reversibility)
- Created new "Time-pressured" Scarcity option for Risk of Rain games
- Classified 22 real games against the framework
- Built frequency analysis showing most/least common options

**Hypothetical Game Designs:**
- Generated 12 imaginary games: 3 archetypal + 9 experimental
- Favorites identified: Loadout (1), Tide Runner (3), Branching Path (4), Expedition (8), Stance Dancer (9), Tide Caller (10), Labyrinth of Choices (11)
- Framework validation revealed invented options (Wagered, Bet-determined, Generationally Earned, etc.)
- Systematic correction: collapsed invented options into existing framework options
- User correction when I over-corrected valid options (Random-varied, Inherited, Legacy)

**New Framework Options Added:**
- Distribution Timing: Partitioned — power segmented, only one segment accessible at a time (stance systems)
- Visibility: Progressive — revealed through exploration/proximity (fog-of-war)

**Experimental Games Frequency Analysis:**
- Compared 9 experimental designs against 22 real games
- Key patterns: experimental games favor Deterministic agency (7/9 vs 2/22), Traded negatives (5/9 vs 0/22), Pre-run timing (5/9 vs 4/22)
- Previously unused options explored: Plateau, Drought/Feast, Dynamic capacity

**Design Space Summary:**
- Wrote 5-paragraph conclusion on unexplored roguelite design territory
- Key insight: experimental games trade randomness for player control
- Identified blind spot: all experimental games use Balanced skill/build ratio

**Blog Post Finalization:**
- Renamed from "A Taxonomy of Roguelite Power Systems" to "Roguelite Design Analysis"
- Added TOC with 6 sections, nav links throughout
- Attribution: "Analysis by Claude (Opus 4.5), direction by a327ex"

**Continuation Session (Log Formatting Fixes):**
- Fixed log rendering by using HTML `<pre><code>` tags inside `<details>` blocks
- marked.js doesn't process markdown inside HTML blocks — raw fences were appearing as literal text
- Added `html_escape()` function to properly escape special characters
- Implemented rewind detection in `jsonl-to-markdown.py` to filter out rewound messages
- Added HTML content detection to wrap pasted HTML in collapsible code blocks instead of blockquotes

Got it. This is a solid design document — 722 lines covering the full game concept from high-level vision down to implementation layers.

**Quick summary of what I read:**

**Core concept:** Minesweeper dungeon navigation + physics auto-battler combat. The cerebral tension of deducing safe paths paired with the spectacle of balls bouncing and colliding with gravity physics.

**The loop:** Navigate grid → use numbers to deduce mines → find valuable rooms → reach boss → physics ball fight → win upgrade → next floor. Single champion ball that evolves throughout the run.

**Resources:** Player HP (dungeon survival, separate from ball combat HP), Gold, Keys, possibly Bombs.

**Room types:** Extensive list inspired by Isaac — mines, shops, treasures, healing, devil/angel deals (mutually exclusive), vaults, gambling, challenge rooms, secrets.

**Implementation layers:** Well-defined from Layer 0 (core physics combat — "make watching two balls fight entertaining") through Layer 6 (content/polish), each with clear exit criteria.

**Open questions explicitly flagged:** Dungeon generation details, combat feel (initial velocity, gravity, arena size), economy (starting resources, prices, drop rates), progression (run length, difficulty curve), meta (starting ball selection, challenge modes).

---

What do you want to brainstorm? Some obvious directions:

1. **Combat mechanics** — What makes ball-on-ball physics fighting actually interesting to watch? Weapon types, damage conditions, special abilities
2. **Dungeon generation** — How do you guarantee "forced gambles" while keeping deduction meaningful? The balance between solvable and gambling
3. **Upgrade/build identity** — What creates distinct "runs" and synergies with a single ball?
4. **The devil/angel and risk/reward systems** — How Isaac's mutually exclusive choices translate here
5. **Something specific** you've been thinking about

Based on my search, here's what I found about Earclacks and the physics ball game:

## Earclacks Physics Ball Simulations

Earclacks is a creator who produces satisfying physics simulation videos.(no content)The community of fans lovingly named the concept in these videos "Weapon Ball."

### The Game Status

Because Earclacks used tags like #simulation and #rpg, many viewers believed a playable "earclacks game" was already available.(no content)While the full game is in development, the official website states they are actively developing an official Earclacks game as a "sophisticated physics sandbox simulator."

### Planned Features

A core feature will be the ability to modify weapon parameters - adjusting damage, speed, weight, and special abilities to create weapon battles.(no content)Players will also be able to create custom arenas and share their creations to challenge friends and the wider community.

### Fan-Made Games

While waiting for the official release, there are some fan-inspired alternatives:

- **BattleBalls** on Steam is a "physics-based arena brawler where you design your own spinning warriors and send it into chaotic fights. Choose your weapon, adjust spin speed, damage, and health."(no content)This game is inspired by Earclacks's ball fight videos but is an original concept by its developers.

- **Weapon Ball Battles** on WebSim is a "gamified version of Earclacks's ball simulations."

- There's also a browser-based "Earclacks-inspired browser game with GENERATED WEAPONS: colorful, bouncing balls in a square arena with spinning weapons."


REMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks.</code></pre>

<details>
<summary><code>WebFetch (https://www.earclacks.com/)</code></summary>

<pre><code># What is Earclacks?

**Earclacks** is a creator known for producing "satisfying physics simulation videos" featuring weapon-based battles. The community dubbed these concept videos "Weapon Ball"—a physics-based battle format.

## The Weapon Ball Concept

The page describes Weapon Ball as showcasing "the unique strengths and weaknesses of each weapon in the Earclacks universe." Battles range from one-on-one duels (Sword vs. Dagger, Staff vs. Spear) to large-scale encounters like Battle Royales and raid boss fights.

## What Makes the Physics Appealing

While the page doesn't explicitly detail the appeal mechanics, it emphasizes that viewers found the videos "mesmerizing" and sought to play them interactively. The draw appears centered on watching realistic physics interactions between different weapons in combat scenarios.

## Battle Mechanics

The page provides limited specifics about actual physics behavior. However, the upcoming official game promises features like:
- Adjustable weapon parameters (damage, speed, weight, special abilities)
- Custom arena design with "physics-altering obstacles"
- Team-based and free-for-all formats

The existing videos demonstrate weapons clashing in controlled physics simulations, though the page doesn't detail specific damage calculations or physics engine behavior beyond mentioning the creator uses #simulation and #rpg tags.</code></pre>

</details>

Got it. Earclacks is a content creator who makes satisfying physics simulation videos featuring "Weapon Balls" — balls equipped with various weapons (swords, daggers, spears, lances, etc.) that fight each other in physics-based battles. The appeal is watching the physics unfold: balls bouncing, weapons clashing, damage being dealt through realistic collisions. The community name "Weapon Ball" emerged from these videos, and they've spawned fan games and an official game in development.

This is clearly the direct inspiration for the physics auto-battler half of Emoji Ball Battles. Let me add this to the document:

     1→# Emoji Ball Battles: Game Design Document

     5→Emoji Ball Battles combines **Minesweeper-style dungeon exploration** with **physics auto-battler combat**. Players navigate a fog-of-war grid using logical deduction to avoid mines and find valuable rooms, then face off in physics-based ball battles at boss rooms.

    10→
    11→**Combat:** The physics ball battles are directly inspired by [Earclacks](https://www.earclacks.com/), a content creator known for satisfying physics simulation videos. The community calls these "Weapon Ball" battles — balls equipped with various weapons (swords, spears, daggers, lances) that bounce around an arena and damage each other through physics collisions. The appeal is watching the physics unfold: unpredictable bounces, weapon clashes, and the tension of HP bars draining. Earclacks' videos range from 1v1 duels to battle royales and raid boss fights, demonstrating how the format scales. The mesmerizing quality of these simulations — where you want to watch "just one more fight" — is the target feeling for Emoji Ball Battles' combat phase.
    12→
    13→**Exploration:** The dungeon navigation draws from classic Minesweeper (logical deduction under uncertainty) and The Binding of Isaac (room variety, resource management, risk/reward room types, devil/angel deal systems).

Done. I added an **Inspirations** subsection to the Overview that:

1. **Explicitly names Earclacks** with a link to their website
2. **Explains the "Weapon Ball" concept** — balls with weapons bouncing and fighting via physics
3. **Captures the appeal** — unpredictable bounces, weapon clashes, HP tension, the "just one more fight" quality
4. **Notes the format's scalability** — 1v1 to battle royales to raid bosses
5. **States the design target** — replicating that mesmerizing simulation quality

I also added a parallel line crediting the exploration inspirations (Minesweeper for deduction, Isaac for room systems) to give both halves of the game proper attribution.

| Method | Shortcut |
|--------|----------|
| **Universal** | `\ + Enter` (backslash then enter) |
| **macOS** | `Option + Enter` |
| **After setup** | `Shift + Enter` (run `/terminal-setup` first) |
| **Control seq** | `Ctrl + J` |

The backslash method (`\` then Enter) works everywhere without any setup.

> OK. The main problem we need to solve is the problem of power choice and power distribution. Most roguelites now have what I call "distributed power choice + distribution". What this means is that players end up choosing their powers in a "choose 3" screen multiple times as the run progresses. There's nothing inherently wrong with this, except for the fact that it is overplayed, many games do it, so something different is necessary. The benefits of doing this is what players are constantly making strategic choices about their builds, it hits the correct choice cadence. The drawbacks are that because you have so many choices, you can usually force the run to always be what you want. Plus, you also have to keep making choices all the time, sometimes you're not in the mood to do that. So the problem we need to solve is moving *away* from distributed power choice and power distribution.
> 
> One way, for instance, is a draft. A draft where you choose all upgrades before the run starts, but where they're distributed at a fixed interval, would be an example of frontloaded power choice and distributed power distribution. This same logic applies to games like "60 seconds", I believe, where you choose the items you'll use throughout the run in the first 60 seconds in a rush. I don't know any games that frontloaded power choice and distribution, but that would be like a draft where you both choose the upgrades/items, and get them from the start of the run, not sure if that'd work. And of course, I'm not sure either if frontloaded power distribution and distributed power choice would work. It also doesn't seem to make sense for either of them to be backloaded, like happening at the end of the run. So it seems the main alternative to distributed power choice and distribution if frontloaded power choice and distributed power distribution. 
> 
> Can you see any alternatives? Try to imagine how games handle their power choice and distribution, and try to classify them along these terms. Perhaps you may even imagine additionnal/better axes of analysis than this one, but start from this since it's the one I've been using for a while.

This is a fascinating design problem. Let me work through it systematically.

---

## Your Current Framework

You've identified two axes:
- **Power Choice**: When do you DECIDE what to get?
- **Power Distribution**: When do you RECEIVE it?

Each can be: Frontloaded, Distributed, or (theoretically) Backloaded

The standard roguelite is **Distributed/Distributed**: choose 1-of-3 repeatedly, get it immediately.

Your identified alternative is **Frontloaded Choice / Distributed Distribution**: draft everything upfront, receive over time.

---

## Testing the Framework Against Games

Let me classify some games and see if the framework holds or needs refinement:

| Game | Choice | Distribution | Notes |
|------|--------|--------------|-------|
| Hades / Isaac / Vampire Survivors | Distributed | Distributed | Standard roguelite |
| Slice & Dice | Frontloaded (party draft) | Frontloaded | You have your party from the start |
| 60 Seconds | Frontloaded (grab phase) | Frontloaded | Rush to grab, then manage |
| Slay the Spire | Distributed | Distributed, then re-distributed (draw) | Two layers! |
| Super Auto Pets / TFT | Distributed | Distributed, but **reversible** | Can sell, reposition |
| Monster Train | Mixed | Mixed | Champion path is frontloaded, cards are distributed |
| XCOM (soldier builds) | Distributed | Distributed | But choices are **permanent per unit** |
| Darkest Dungeon | Distributed | Distributed | But upgrades are **persistent across runs** |
| FTL | Distributed | Immediate | Low agency (find what you find), high choice on USE |
| Into the Breach | Frontloaded (team select) | Frontloaded | Pilots distributed via rescue |

This reveals some issues with the two-axis model. A few games don't fit cleanly because there are **hidden variables**.

---

## Proposed Additional Axes

### 1. Agency (How much control over WHAT?)

- **High agency**: Choose exactly what you want (pick 1 of 3)
- **Medium agency**: Influence the pool (rerolls, shops, build-around)
- **Low agency**: Take what you find (random drops, no choice)

FTL is **Distributed/Distributed** but feels different from Hades because it's **low agency** — you find what you find, and your choice is whether to BUY it, not what appears.

### 2. Reversibility (Can you change your mind?)

- **Permanent**: Once taken, forever (Isaac items, Slay the Spire cards)
- **Swappable**: Equip/unequip, limited slots (Diablo gear, TFT units)
- **Consumable**: Use once and gone (potions, scrolls)

Super Auto Pets is Distributed/Distributed but feels different because you can SELL units. You're not locked in. The "forcing runs" problem you mentioned is partially solved by reversibility — you can pivot.

### 3. Commitment Granularity (How big are the choices?)

- **Macro choices**: Class, faction, pact — defines everything downstream
- **Micro choices**: Individual items, small upgrades

Monster Train's champion upgrades are a MACRO frontloaded choice that filters your distributed MICRO choices. You make one big commitment, then small choices within that lane.

### 4. Visibility (How much do you see before choosing?)

- **Full visibility**: See all options, choose what you can afford
- **Partial visibility**: See some options (the current 3), others hidden
- **No visibility**: Blind picks, discover what you got

Standard roguelite is partial visibility. A shop with all items priced is full visibility. A gacha pull is no visibility.

---

## Alternative Structures

Now let me brainstorm structures that are distinctly NOT "distributed choice + distributed distribution":

### Structure A: Frontloaded Identity + Filtered Distribution

**Example**: You pick a "path" or "archetype" at run start. This doesn't give you powers directly, but FILTERS what can appear. Throughout the run, you get random upgrades from your filtered pool — no choices, just acquisition.

- Choice: Frontloaded (one big decision)
- Distribution: Distributed (random over time)
- Agency: High at start, zero after

**Why it might work**: One meaningful choice with consequences. No decision fatigue mid-run. Runs feel different because of the initial commitment, not because you "forced" them.

### Structure B: Economic/Market System

**Example**: All upgrades are visible in a shop. You have limited currency. You buy what you want when you can afford it. Prices might fluctuate or there's competition.

- Choice: Distributed (buy decisions)
- Distribution: Immediate (buy = receive)
- But feels different because: Full visibility, resource constraint is the limit, not option scarcity

**Why it might work**: The choice isn't "which of these 3?" but "can I afford what I want, and is it worth the cost?" Different decision calculus.

### Structure C: Evolution/Mutation System

**Example**: You start with base abilities. They TRANSFORM based on how you use them or what happens in battles. Use your sword a lot, it becomes sharper. Take fire damage, gain fire resistance.

- Choice: Implicit (playstyle determines evolution)
- Distribution: Distributed (happens as you play)
- Agency: Indirect (you influence, not select)

**Why it might work**: No menus. No "choose 1 of 3." Power grows organically from play. The Tamagotchi effect — your ball becomes YOUR ball through how it lived.

### Structure D: Inheritance/Legacy System

**Example**: Your ball dies, but passes some traits to the next ball. Or: You have multiple balls, and defeated balls pass their essence to survivors.

- Choice: Distributed (which traits to protect/pass)
- Distribution: Distributed (on death/transition)
- Novel axis: Power comes from LOSS, not gain

**Why it might work**: Inverts the standard progression. Loss is meaningful, not just failure.

### Structure E: Loadout + Permutation System

**Example**: Before each fight, you choose a loadout from your acquired upgrades. You have 10 upgrades but can only equip 4. Different fights want different loadouts.

- Acquisition: Distributed (find upgrades over run)
- Equip Choice: Distributed (before each fight)
- But: Reversible and contextual

**Why it might work**: Collection grows, but you're making tactical choices about APPLICATION, not acquisition. The "choose 1 of 3" becomes "which of MY things do I use NOW?"

### Structure F: Inverse Progression (Degradation)

**Example**: Start with a powerful ball. Throughout the run, you LOSE abilities as you take damage or make sacrifices. Choice becomes "what do I protect?" not "what do I add?"

- Choice: Distributed (protect/sacrifice decisions)
- Distribution: Negative distributed (loss over time)

**Why it might work**: Completely inverts the power fantasy. Desperate, tense. Every fight costs something. Different emotional arc.

### Structure G: Draft with Opponent

**Example**: Both you and the enemy draft from the same pool. You see what they're building. Counter-drafting, hate-drafting, reading their strategy.

- Choice: Frontloaded (draft phase)
- Distribution: Frontloaded or distributed
- Novel axis: Competitive/interactive choice

**Why it might work**: The choice isn't "what's best for me?" but "what's best given what they're doing?" Social/strategic layer even in single-player.

---

## Axis Refinement Summary

Your original two axes are useful, but I'd propose expanding to:

1. **Choice Timing**: Frontloaded / Distributed / Backloaded
2. **Distribution Timing**: Frontloaded / Distributed / Backloaded  
3. **Agency Level**: High (select) / Medium (influence) / Low (random)
4. **Reversibility**: Permanent / Swappable / Consumable
5. **Visibility**: Full / Partial / None
6. **Commitment Granularity**: Macro (few big) / Micro (many small)
7. **Polarity**: Additive (gain power) / Subtractive (lose power)

The standard roguelite is: **Distributed, Distributed, High Agency, Permanent, Partial Visibility, Micro, Additive**.

Moving away means changing one or more of these axes significantly.

---

## For Emoji Ball Battles Specifically

Given that the core is an AUTO-battler where you WATCH physics unfold, the spectacle is the payoff. Your agency isn't in the fight — it's in the SETUP. This suggests:

- **Frontloaded choice makes thematic sense**: You prepare your ball, then watch it fight
- **The draft could BE the game**: The interesting decisions happen before combat
- **Low mid-fight agency**: Once balls are in the arena, physics takes over

A draft system (frontloaded choice, distributed distribution) seems natural here. But to make it feel distinct from standard roguelites, you could combine it with:

- **Opponent drafting** (competitive, reading the enemy)
- **Evolution** (your draft influences growth direction, not exact outcomes)
- **Loadout switching** (collect many upgrades, equip few per fight)
- **Degradation** (start strong, protect what matters)

What resonates? Or should I dig deeper into any of these directions?

> I like the loadout idea the most. However, before that, I *really* like your addition of agency, reversibility, etc. Could you perhaps run a deeper analysis of roguelites and classify all of them on these axes, as well as any other axes you find? I don't care how long it takes, I just want a pretty thorough exploration. ultrathink

This is exactly the kind of deep dive I enjoy. Let me build a comprehensive taxonomy and then classify a wide range of roguelites against it.

---

## Comprehensive Axis Framework

I'll organize these into categories: **Acquisition**, **Management**, **Information**, **Progression**, and **Meta**.

---

### ACQUISITION AXES

These govern HOW and WHEN you get power.

#### 1. Choice Timing
*When do you make decisions about what powers to pursue?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Pre-run** | Before the run starts (loadout, character, draft) | Into the Breach team selection |
| **Early-run** | Concentrated in opening phase | Slice & Dice party draft |
| **Distributed** | Spread throughout the run | Hades boon choices |
| **Milestone** | At specific progression points | Monster Train champion upgrades |
| **Reactive** | In response to situations (find, then decide) | FTL event choices |
| **Continuous** | Constant stream of micro-decisions | TFT shop every round |

#### 2. Distribution Timing
*When do powers become available to use?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Immediate** | Get it, use it now | Most action roguelites |
| **Delayed-Random** | Acquired but randomly accessible | Deckbuilder card draw |
| **Delayed-Sequential** | Acquired but unlocks over time | Skill trees with prerequisites |
| **Conditional** | Available when conditions met | Isaac's activated items (charge) |
| **Frontloaded** | Have everything from the start | Into the Breach mechs |

#### 3. Agency
*How much control over WHAT you get?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Deterministic** | Choose exactly what you want | Shop with fixed inventory |
| **Curated** | Choose from limited options | Pick 1 of 3 |
| **Influenced** | Affect the pool/probabilities | Class filters available items |
| **Serendipitous** | Find what you find | FTL random events |
| **Predetermined** | Fixed for this run, no choice | Daily challenge seeds |

#### 4. Negative Acquisition
*Do you gain negatives alongside positives?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **None** | Pure power growth | Vampire Survivors |
| **Optional** | Can choose to take risks | Devil deals in Isaac |
| **Coupled** | Positives come with negatives | Parasites in Returnal |
| **Forced** | Negatives accumulate regardless | Corruption in Curse of the Dead Gods |
| **Traded** | Must sacrifice to gain | Darkest Dungeon stress |

---

### MANAGEMENT AXES

These govern how you HANDLE power once acquired.

#### 5. Reversibility
*Can you undo or change power choices?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Permanent** | Locked in forever | Isaac passive items |
| **Transformable** | Can evolve/upgrade but not remove | Card upgrades in Slay the Spire |
| **Removable** | Can discard/destroy | Card removal events |
| **Swappable** | Equip/unequip, limited slots | Dead Cells weapon slots |
| **Sellable** | Trade back for resources | Super Auto Pets selling units |
| **Fluid** | Continuous reorganization | Backpack Hero spatial arrangement |

#### 6. Capacity
*How many powers can you have?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Unlimited** | Stack everything | Risk of Rain 2 item stacking |
| **Soft cap** | Diminishing returns or dilution | Deckbuilders (bigger deck = less consistency) |
| **Hard cap** | Fixed slots | Vampire Survivors (6 weapons, 6 passives) |
| **Contextual** | Different limits for different types | Isaac (unlimited passives, 1-2 actives) |
| **Dynamic** | Capacity itself can change | Backpack size upgrades |

#### 7. Interaction
*How do powers relate to each other?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Independent** | Each stands alone | Simple stat boosts |
| **Synergistic** | Combinations provide bonuses | Isaac item synergies |
| **Exclusive** | Some lock out others | Devil/Angel room exclusivity |
| **Hierarchical** | Prerequisites, skill trees | Traditional RPG skill trees |
| **Competitive** | Powers vie for limited resource | Mana/energy allocation |
| **Systemic** | Complex emergent interactions | Noita spell combinations |

#### 8. Upgrade Depth
*How much can individual powers grow?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Flat** | Acquired at full power | Most Isaac items |
| **Linear** | Can upgrade incrementally | Hades boon levels |
| **Branching** | Choose upgrade path | Monster Train champion paths |
| **Infinite** | Keep stacking/improving | Risk of Rain 2 item stacking |
| **Evolutionary** | Transforms into something else | Vampire Survivors weapon evolutions |

---

### INFORMATION AXES

These govern what you KNOW about power.

#### 9. Visibility
*What can you see about available powers?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Complete** | See all possibilities in the game | Into the Breach (all teams visible) |
| **Pool-visible** | See what's possible this run | TFT (know the unit pool) |
| **Forecast** | See upcoming options | Hades door previews, Curse of the Dead Gods paths |
| **Present** | See current options only | Standard pick 1 of 3 |
| **Obscured** | Some information hidden | Unknown item effects until used |
| **Blind** | No information | Gacha pulls, mystery boxes |

#### 10. Comprehension
*Do you understand what powers do?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Transparent** | Clear, predictable effects | Hades boon descriptions |
| **Calculable** | Effects clear but require math | Balatro multiplier calculations |
| **Learnable** | Must discover through experience | Isaac (hundreds of items, complex interactions) |
| **Opaque** | Hard to evaluate even with knowledge | Noita wand mechanics |
| **Unknown** | Must discover what it even does | Unidentified items, Isaac pills |

---

### PROGRESSION AXES

These govern how power CHANGES over time.

#### 11. Growth Pattern
*How does total power change through the run?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Additive** | Monotonically gaining | Most roguelites |
| **Multiplicative** | Exponential scaling | Risk of Rain 2 late-game |
| **Subtractive** | Losing over time | Stress/permadeath in Darkest Dungeon |
| **Transformative** | Changing form, not necessarily growing | Build pivots in TFT |
| **Oscillating** | Power ebbs and flows | Loop Hero (stronger each loop, but so is world) |
| **Plateau** | Diminishing returns, power cap | Some balanced roguelites |

#### 12. Pacing
*When do upgrade opportunities occur?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Fixed interval** | Every N rooms/waves/minutes | Vampire Survivors level-ups |
| **Performance-based** | Better play = more upgrades | Skill-gated rewards |
| **Resource-gated** | Spend currency to upgrade | Shops, FTL scrap |
| **Event-triggered** | Tied to specific encounters | Boss rewards |
| **Player-controlled** | Choose when to upgrade | Strategic timing of purchases |
| **Continuous** | Constant small increments | Idle game mechanics |

#### 13. Difficulty Coupling
*How does difficulty relate to power?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Fixed** | Difficulty doesn't scale with power | Fixed enemy stats |
| **Time-scaled** | Difficulty increases over time regardless | Risk of Rain 2 difficulty timer |
| **Power-scaled** | Difficulty responds to player power | Adaptive difficulty |
| **Player-chosen** | Player controls difficulty | Heat system in Hades |
| **Oscillating** | Difficulty varies deliberately | Easy/hard areas in sequence |

---

### META AXES

These govern persistence and starting conditions.

#### 14. Persistence
*What carries between runs?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Nothing** | Pure roguelike | Traditional roguelikes |
| **Unlocks** | New options become available | Most roguelites |
| **Upgrades** | Permanent stat increases | Hades Mirror |
| **Resources** | Currency/materials carry over | Darkest Dungeon gold |
| **Progress** | Story/world changes | Hades story, Cult of the Lamb cult |
| **Legacy** | Previous runs affect future runs | Some elements in Rogue Legacy |

#### 15. Starting Variance
*How different are run starts?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Identical** | Always same start | Pure starting position |
| **Character-varied** | Different characters/classes | Most roguelites |
| **Loadout-varied** | Choose starting gear | Hades keepsakes, weapons |
| **Random-varied** | Random starting conditions | Random starting items |
| **Seeded** | Deterministic based on seed | Daily challenges |
| **Inherited** | Based on previous run | Rogue Legacy traits |

#### 16. Run Identity
*When does a run's "build" crystallize?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Pre-determined** | Identity set before run | Character choice is everything |
| **Early-crystallizing** | First few choices define run | Monster Train champion path |
| **Emergent** | Identity emerges from opportunities | Isaac "became a poison build" |
| **Fluid** | Can pivot throughout | TFT reroll compositions |
| **Convergent** | All runs approach similar end state | Limited viable builds |

---

## Additional Axes Discovered Through Analysis

While classifying, I found several more axes that differentiate games:

### 17. Skill vs Build Ratio
*What matters more for success?*

| Value | Example |
|-------|---------|
| **Execution-dominant** | Spelunky (items help but skill dominates) |
| **Build-dominant** | Vampire Survivors (right build plays itself) |
| **Balanced** | Hades, Slay the Spire |
| **Knowledge-dominant** | Isaac (knowing item interactions matters most) |

### 18. Decision Density
*How many meaningful decisions per unit time?*

| Value | Example |
|-------|---------|
| **Sparse** | Vampire Survivors (occasional level-up) |
| **Moderate** | Hades (one choice per room) |
| **Dense** | TFT (constant shop/positioning decisions) |
| **Continuous** | Real-time tactical games |

### 19. Commitment Weight
*How heavy does each choice feel?*

| Value | Example |
|-------|---------|
| **Light** | Super Auto Pets (can sell immediately) |
| **Medium** | Hades (permanent but many opportunities) |
| **Heavy** | Monster Train champion path (defines the run) |
| **Critical** | Into the Breach team choice |

### 20. Information Asymmetry
*Does the game know more than you?*

| Value | Example |
|-------|---------|
| **Symmetric** | Into the Breach (see enemy intent) |
| **Learnable asymmetry** | Isaac (can learn all item effects) |
| **Permanent asymmetry** | Hidden dice rolls, RNG you can't see |
| **Adversarial** | Game actively hides/misleads (rare) |

### 21. Power Source Diversity
*Where does power come from?*

| Value | Example |
|-------|---------|
| **Single source** | Vampire Survivors (just upgrades) |
| **Dual source** | Hades (boons + weapon aspects) |
| **Multi-source** | Isaac (items + pills + cards + trinkets + stats) |
| **Interconnected** | Darkest Dungeon (heroes + trinkets + skills + provisions + stress) |

### 22. Failure Mode
*What happens when things go wrong?*

| Value | Example |
|-------|---------|
| **Binary death** | Most roguelites (HP hits 0, run ends) |
| **Degradation** | Darkest Dungeon (stress, afflictions, retreat) |
| **Setback** | TFT (lose health, continue playing) |
| **Transformation** | Some games turn failure into different play |

---

## Pattern Analysis

### Cluster 1: "The Standard Model"
**Distributed + Curated + Permanent + Additive**

Games: Hades, Isaac, Gungeon, Nuclear Throne, most action roguelites

This is the default. You play, you're offered choices, you pick, you keep what you pick, you get stronger. It works because:
- Constant engagement (always another choice coming)
- Clear progression (number go up)
- Build identity emerges (you become "the poison guy")

**The problem you identified**: Too much control. Skilled players force builds. Decision fatigue for some.

### Cluster 2: "The Deckbuilder"
**Distributed + Curated + Removable + Delayed-Random**

Games: Slay the Spire, Monster Train, Balatro

Adds a second layer: acquisition vs. access. You choose what enters your deck, but RNG determines when you draw it. This creates:
- Strategic depth (deck composition matters)
- Variance within consistency (same deck, different draws)
- Active pruning decisions (removal is as important as addition)

### Cluster 3: "The Auto-battler"
**Continuous + Curated + Sellable + Hard cap + Oscillating**

Games: TFT, Super Auto Pets, Dota Underlords

Key innovations:
- **Sellable** changes everything. You're not committing, you're investing. Pivoting is core skill.
- **Hard cap** forces replacement decisions, not just addition
- **Oscillating** power (win streaks, loss streaks, power spikes) creates drama
- **Shared pool** (in competitive) adds read/counter-play

### Cluster 4: "The Frontloaded Tactician"
**Pre-run + Frontloaded + Deterministic + Hard cap**

Games: Into the Breach, (partially) Slice & Dice

You make THE choice before playing. The run is about executing with what you chose. This creates:
- Heavy commitment weight (choice matters enormously)
- Mastery depth (learn your tools deeply)
- Less "build emerged from RNG," more "I chose this build"

### Cluster 5: "The Survivor-like"
**Distributed + Curated + Permanent + Hard cap + Low decision density**

Games: Vampire Survivors, Brotato, Halls of Torment

Simplifies to:
- Fewer, less frequent decisions
- Hard cap forces build identity
- Spectacle over strategy (watching your build work)
- Evolution/transformation as goal (not just "more power")

### Cluster 6: "The Systems Sandbox"
**Reactive + Serendipitous + Swappable + Systemic**

Games: Noita, (partially) Caves of Qud

Emphasizes:
- Emergent interactions over designed synergies
- Discovery and experimentation
- Player creativity in combining systems
- "What if I try..." is the core engagement

---

## Underexplored Design Space

Based on this analysis, here are combinations that are RARE or ABSENT:

### 1. Subtractive Primary Growth
Almost all roguelites are additive (gain power). What if:
- You start with everything
- Run is about what you LOSE
- Each fight/choice costs something
- Victory is surviving with enough left

Only Darkest Dungeon touches this (stress, death), but it's still primarily additive (you're building up your roster/estate).

### 2. Backloaded Choice
No games do this. Potential version:
- Play the run with random acquisitions
- At the end, choose what to KEEP for next run
- Retroactive build-crafting

### 3. Oscillating as Core (not side effect)
Loop Hero gestures at this. But what if power explicitly went UP and DOWN as the primary rhythm? 
- Spend power to progress
- Regenerate through specific actions
- Manage your power curve, not just build it

### 4. Blind Acquisition + Revealed Over Time
You get items but don't know what they do until you use them in specific situations. Currently only consumables (pills) work this way. What if core upgrades did?

### 5. Competitive Draft (Single-player)
You and an AI opponent draft from the same pool. Hate-drafting, counter-picking, reading their build. Games like Teamfight Tactics have shared pools but not direct drafting.

### 6. Loadout Swapping Within Run
Collect many upgrades, equip few, swap between fights. Common in non-roguelike RPGs (equipment), rare in roguelites. Forces "right tool for the job" decisions.

### 7. Inherited/Evolutionary Growth
Power doesn't come from items, comes from what you DO. Use fire a lot → become fire-attuned. Kill enemies with crits → crit chance increases. Implicit choice through behavior.

### 8. Full Visibility + Scarcity
See EVERYTHING that could appear in your run from the start. But you can only afford/access some. Shifts from "what will I find?" to "what should I prioritize?"

---

## For Emoji Ball Battles: The Loadout Angle

You mentioned liking the loadout idea. Let me map what that would look like using this framework:

**Proposed Structure:**
- **Choice Timing**: Distributed (collect throughout) + Pre-fight (equip for each battle)
- **Distribution Timing**: Immediate (get it when you acquire it)
- **Agency**: Serendipitous or Curated (find/buy upgrades) + Deterministic (choose loadout)
- **Reversibility**: Swappable (loadout), but permanent collection
- **Capacity**: Unlimited collection, Hard cap loadout
- **Interaction**: Synergistic (loadout combos)
- **Visibility**: Complete (see your whole collection)
- **Growth**: Additive (collection grows) + Contextual (power in any fight = loadout)

**What this creates:**
- Collection is the meta-progression within a run
- Each fight is a puzzle: "which of my tools work here?"
- Build identity is per-fight, not per-run
- Finding new upgrades expands OPTIONS, not direct power
- The "forcing runs" problem dissolves — you can't force a fight, only prepare for it

**Comparison to existing games:**
- Like an RPG equipment system (Diablo) but within a roguelike run
- Like TFT's positioning decisions but for loadout composition
- Like Monster Hunter's "prepare for the hunt" loop

This is relatively unexplored in roguelites. Most games with "swappable" are action games swapping weapons mid-combat (Dead Cells), not strategic loadout decisions between encounters.

---

Do you want me to dig deeper into the loadout concept specifically, or explore any of the other underexplored spaces?

My recommendation would be **"A Taxonomy of Roguelite Power Systems"** — it's clear about what the post delivers and has a slight academic flavor that fits the systematic analysis.

> Could you format these like the other ones? The other ones also have a column with their description, it's harder to understand what you mean without that description.

### 17. Skill vs Build Ratio
*What matters more for success?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Execution-dominant** | Player skill matters most, build is secondary | Spelunky (items help but skill dominates) |
| **Build-dominant** | Right build matters most, execution is secondary | Vampire Survivors (right build plays itself) |
| **Balanced** | Both contribute meaningfully | Hades, Slay the Spire |
| **Knowledge-dominant** | Knowing interactions/mechanics matters most | Isaac (knowing item interactions matters most) |

### 18. Decision Density
*How many meaningful decisions per unit time?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Sparse** | Infrequent decisions, long gaps between | Vampire Survivors (occasional level-up) |
| **Moderate** | Regular rhythm of choices | Hades (one choice per room) |
| **Dense** | Frequent, overlapping decisions | TFT (constant shop/positioning decisions) |
| **Continuous** | Always deciding, no discrete moments | Real-time tactical games |

### 19. Commitment Weight
*How heavy does each choice feel?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Light** | Easy to undo or replace, low stakes per choice | Super Auto Pets (can sell immediately) |
| **Medium** | Permanent but many opportunities to choose | Hades (permanent but many opportunities) |
| **Heavy** | Few choices, each shapes the run significantly | Monster Train champion path (defines the run) |
| **Critical** | One or two choices determine everything | Into the Breach team choice |

### 20. Information Asymmetry
*Does the game know more than you?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Symmetric** | Player sees everything the game uses | Into the Breach (see enemy intent) |
| **Learnable asymmetry** | Hidden info exists but can be memorized | Isaac (can learn all item effects) |
| **Permanent asymmetry** | Some information always hidden from player | Hidden dice rolls, RNG you can't see |
| **Adversarial** | Game actively conceals or misleads | Game actively hides/misleads (rare) |

### 21. Power Source Diversity
*Where does power come from?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Single source** | One system provides all power | Vampire Survivors (just upgrades) |
| **Dual source** | Two distinct systems contribute | Hades (boons + weapon aspects) |
| **Multi-source** | Several independent power systems | Isaac (items + pills + cards + trinkets + stats) |
| **Interconnected** | Multiple systems that affect each other | Darkest Dungeon (heroes + trinkets + skills + provisions + stress) |

### 22. Failure Mode
*What happens when things go wrong?*

| Value | Description | Example |
|-------|-------------|---------|
| **Binary death** | Single failure state ends the run | Most roguelites (HP hits 0, run ends) |
| **Degradation** | Failures accumulate, weakening you over time | Darkest Dungeon (stress, afflictions, retreat) |
| **Setback** | Failure costs progress but run continues | TFT (lose health, continue playing) |
| **Transformation** | Failure changes how you play rather than ending | Some games turn failure into different play |

> 17, 18, 19 and 21 are valid. 20 and 22 do not feel like they're valid. Would you like to defend 20 and 22 as valid?

You're right to challenge them. Let me try to defend, and if I can't, I'll concede.

**Axis 20: Information Asymmetry**

My defense would be: it affects how you *choose* power. If you don't know what an item does (Isaac pills, unidentified items), your choice is degraded. If you can see enemy intent (Into the Breach), you can choose power that counters it.

But honestly — this overlaps heavily with **Axis 10: Comprehension** (do you understand what powers do?) and **Axis 9: Visibility** (what can you see about available powers?). Information Asymmetry as I framed it is broader than power systems — it's about game information in general (enemy behavior, hidden RNG, etc.). That's scope creep.

**Verdict: Not valid as a distinct power system axis.** It's either redundant with 9/10 or too broad.

---

**Axis 22: Failure Mode**

My defense would be: failure mode affects how you *relate* to your power investments. Binary death means your build either worked or it didn't. Degradation means your build erodes. Setback means you can recover.

But honestly — this is about consequences of losing, not about how power is chosen, distributed, or managed. It's adjacent to power systems (Darkest Dungeon's stress *does* affect power), but the axis as framed is about failure structure generally, not power specifically.

**Verdict: Not valid.** It's a general game design axis, not a power system axis.

---

I concede both. 17, 18, 19, and 21 stand. 20 and 22 are out.

<pre><code>1→# A Taxonomy of Roguelite Power Systems
     2→
     3→Most roguelites use what could be called "distributed power choice + distribution" — players choose their powers in a "choose 1 of 3" screen multiple times as the run progresses. There's nothing inherently wrong with this, except that it's overplayed. The benefits: players constantly make strategic choices about their builds, hitting the correct choice cadence. The drawbacks: because you have so many choices, you can usually force the run to always be what you want. Plus, you have to keep making choices all the time — sometimes you're not in the mood.
     4→
     5→This analysis attempts to map the full possibility space of how roguelites handle power acquisition and management, using a multi-axis framework.
     6→
     7→---
     8→
     9→## The Framework
    10→
    11→I'll organize these into categories: **Acquisition**, **Management**, **Information**, **Progression**, and **Meta**.
    12→
    13→---
    14→
    15→## ACQUISITION AXES
    16→
    17→These govern HOW and WHEN you get power.
    18→
    19→### 1. Choice Timing
    20→*When do you make decisions about what powers to pursue?*
    21→
    22→| Value | Description | Example |
    23→|-------|-------------|---------|
    24→| **Pre-run** | Before the run starts (loadout, character, draft) | Into the Breach team selection |
    25→| **Early-run** | Concentrated in opening phase | Slice &amp; Dice party draft |
    26→| **Distributed** | Spread throughout the run | Hades boon choices |
    27→| **Milestone** | At specific progression points | Monster Train champion upgrades |
    28→| **Reactive** | In response to situations (find, then decide) | FTL event choices |
    29→| **Continuous** | Constant stream of micro-decisions | TFT shop every round |
    30→

> Alright, given these 20 axes, do you feel any of them are redundant, unnecessary? Do you feel the categories are correct?

Let me think through this critically.

---

## Potentially Redundant Axes

**16. Run Identity** — I suspect this is derivable from other axes rather than independent.

- Pre-run Choice Timing + Permanent Reversibility → Pre-determined identity
- Distributed Choice Timing + Permanent Reversibility → Emergent identity  
- Distributed Choice Timing + Sellable Reversibility → Fluid identity

Run Identity seems to be a *consequence* of Choice Timing × Reversibility, not an independent dimension. If you know those two, you can predict Run Identity.

**19. Commitment Weight** — Similarly derivable.

- Permanent Reversibility + Sparse Decision Density → Heavy commitment
- Sellable Reversibility + Dense Decision Density → Light commitment

Commitment Weight ≈ Reversibility × (inverse of Decision Density). It's how the combination *feels*, not an independent axis.

**18. Decision Density** — Partially overlaps with Pacing (12).

Pacing describes *when* opportunities occur. Decision Density describes *how often* you're deciding. In most games these correlate directly. The distinction would be if you make multiple decisions per opportunity, but that's rare enough that it might not warrant a separate axis.

---

## Potentially Tangential Axes

**13. Difficulty Coupling** — This is about challenge design, not power systems. It affects how power *feels* (if difficulty scales, your power gains feel less impactful), but it's not about how power is chosen, distributed, or managed. Similar to the axes we rejected (Information Asymmetry, Failure Mode).

**17. Skill vs Build Ratio** — This is about what matters for *success*, not about power systems themselves. A game could have identical power systems but different skill/build ratios based on combat design. It's important for game feel but tangential to power architecture.

---

## Category Issues

**Pacing (12)** feels misplaced in Progression. It's about *when opportunities occur*, which is closer to Acquisition than to how power changes over time. Growth Pattern (11) and Difficulty Coupling (13) are about change over time, but Pacing is about timing of opportunities.

**Experience Axes** as a category feels awkward. These axes describe emergent properties (how it *feels*) rather than structural properties (how it *works*). If they're derivable from structural axes, they might not belong in the framework at all — or they belong in a separate "derived properties" section rather than as primary axes.

---

## My Recommendation

**Keep (clearly independent and structural):**
1. Choice Timing
2. Distribution Timing  
3. Agency
4. Negative Acquisition
5. Reversibility
6. Capacity
7. Interaction
8. Upgrade Depth
9. Visibility
10. Comprehension
11. Growth Pattern
14. Persistence
15. Starting Variance
20. Power Source Diversity

**Cut or demote to "derived properties":**
- 12. Pacing (merge with Choice Timing or cut — they're closely related)
- 13. Difficulty Coupling (tangential)
- 16. Run Identity (derivable from 1 + 5)
- 17. Skill vs Build Ratio (tangential)
- 18. Decision Density (derivable from Pacing)
- 19. Commitment Weight (derivable from 5 + 18)

That would leave **14-15 core axes** that are truly independent structural dimensions.

---

What's your take? Do you see value in keeping the "derived" axes as a separate section (useful for describing games even if not independent), or should they be cut entirely?

> I think pacing is the more specific examples of how choice timing happens, but that's useful information to have under such analysis. So maybe add it as a subtable bellow choice timing. Perhaps that should be the solution for all others where the same problem occurs? I agree that Difficulty Coupling should likely be removed, this is a more general game design thing than power system necessarily. I think Run Identity is useful and should be kept. I think Skill vs Build is also important, as even though it isn't about power itself, it's about how runs feel to play. I agree Decision Density should be removed. Commitment WEight should be a subtable of 5, as it has some overlap but it's slightly different in a useful way.

That makes sense. So the structure becomes:

**Changes:**
- Pacing → subtable under Choice Timing (how the timing manifests)
- Commitment Weight → subtable under Reversibility (how reversibility feels)
- Remove Difficulty Coupling
- Remove Decision Density
- Keep Run Identity
- Keep Skill vs Build Ratio

**New structure (16 axes):**

1. Choice Timing (+ Pacing subtable)
2. Distribution Timing
3. Agency
4. Negative Acquisition
5. Reversibility (+ Commitment Weight subtable)
6. Capacity
7. Interaction
8. Upgrade Depth
9. Visibility
10. Comprehension
11. Growth Pattern

13. Starting Variance
14. Run Identity
15. Skill vs Build Ratio
16. Power Source Diversity

Should I update the document with this structure now?

> Yes. Unless you think it needs further changes. Please run another analysis if you think anything still needs merging or removal or additions.

Let me do a final pass.

**One issue:** After removing Decision Density, the Experience category has two axes that don't really belong together:
- **Skill vs Build Ratio** — about player experience, what matters for success
- **Power Source Diversity** — about system architecture, where power comes from

Power Source Diversity is structural, not experiential. It should probably move to **Management** (it's about the structure of what you're managing).

**Resulting category sizes:**
- Acquisition: 4
- Management: 5 (with Power Source Diversity)
- Information: 2
- Progression: 1 (just Growth Pattern)
- Meta: 3
- Experience: 1 (just Skill vs Build Ratio)

Having single-axis categories (Progression, Experience) is slightly awkward but the axes themselves are valid and distinct. I don't think we should cut them or force-merge them somewhere they don't belong.

**One potential addition:** I noticed we don't have an axis for **Scarcity** — are power options abundant or rare? This is different from:
- Capacity (how many you can hold)
- Pacing (when opportunities occur)
- Agency (control over what you get)

Examples:
- **Abundant**: Vampire Survivors (constant stream)
- **Scarce**: FTL (limited scrap, must prioritize)
- **Competitive**: TFT (shared pool)

But this might overlap enough with existing axes that it's not necessary. Your call on whether to add it.

---

**My recommendation:** Proceed with 16 axes, move Power Source Diversity to Management, accept the single-axis categories. Skip Scarcity unless you feel it's missing.

Should I update the document with this structure?

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/website/notes/A Taxonomy of Roguelite Power Systems.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
     1→# A Taxonomy of Roguelite Power Systems
     2→
     3→Most roguelites use what could be called "distributed power choice + distribution" — players choose their powers in a "choose 1 of 3" screen multiple times as the run progresses. There's nothing inherently wrong with this, except that it's overplayed. The benefits: players constantly make strategic choices about their builds, hitting the correct choice cadence. The drawbacks: because you have so many choices, you can usually force the run to always be what you want. Plus, you have to keep making choices all the time — sometimes you're not in the mood.
     4→
     5→This analysis attempts to map the full possibility space of how roguelites handle power acquisition and management, using a multi-axis framework.
     6→
     7→---
     8→
     9→## The Framework
    10→
    11→The axes are organized into categories: **Acquisition**, **Management**, **Information**, **Progression**, **Meta**, and **Experience**.
    12→
    13→---
    14→
    15→## ACQUISITION AXES
    16→
    17→These govern HOW and WHEN you get power.
    18→
    19→### 1. Choice Timing
    20→*When do you make decisions about what powers to pursue?*
    21→
    22→| Value | Description | Example |
    23→|-------|-------------|---------|
    24→| **Pre-run** | Before the run starts (loadout, character, draft) | Into the Breach team selection |
    25→| **Early-run** | Concentrated in opening phase | Slice &amp; Dice party draft |
    26→| **Distributed** | Spread throughout the run | Hades boon choices |
    27→| **Milestone** | At specific progression points | Monster Train champion upgrades |
    28→| **Reactive** | In response to situations (find, then decide) | FTL event choices |
    29→| **Continuous** | Constant stream of micro-decisions | TFT shop every round |
... [233 more lines]</code></pre>

---

## The Binding of Isaac (Repentance)

**1. Choice Timing:** Distributed + Reactive
- You make choices throughout the run, but often in response to what appears
- **Pacing:** Event-triggered (room clears, boss kills) + Resource-gated (shops require coins)

**2. Distribution Timing:** Immediate + Conditional
- Most items work instantly when picked up
- Active items require charges (Conditional)

**3. Agency:** Serendipitous + Curated + Influenced
- Room drops are random (Serendipitous)
- Shops, devil/angel rooms offer choices (Curated)
- Some items affect item pools (Influenced)

**4. Negative Acquisition:** Optional + Coupled + Forced
- Devil deals cost HP (Optional)
- Some items have downsides (Coupled - e.g., Soy Milk)
- Curses can be forced (Forced)

**5. Scarcity:** Moderate
- Enough items to build around, but can't take everything; key/coin constraints

**6. Reversibility:** Permanent + Transformable
- Most items are permanent once taken
- Reroll machines and D6 allow transformation
- **Commitment Weight:** Medium to Heavy — permanent choices, but many opportunities per run

**7. Capacity:** Contextual
- Unlimited passive items
- 1-2 active item slots (depending on items like Schoolbag)
- Limited consumable slots (cards, pills, runes)

**8. Interaction:** Highly Synergistic + Exclusive
- Items combo in complex, sometimes unexpected ways
- Devil/Angel exclusivity (taking devil deals locks angel rooms)

**9. Upgrade Depth:** Flat + some Transformable
- Most items are at full power when acquired
- Birthright can transform character-specific items
- Some items upgrade others (e.g., BFFS! affects familiars)

**10. Power Source Diversity:** Multi-source
- Passive items, active items, pills, cards, runes, trinkets, character stats, tainted character mechanics

**11. Visibility:** Present + Obscured
- See what's in the current room
- Secret rooms hidden; item effects not shown for new players (unless you use external resources)

**12. Comprehension:** Learnable + Unknown
- Hundreds of items requiring experience to understand
- Pills are unknown until identified each run
- Complex interactions not documented in-game

**13. Growth Pattern:** Additive + Transformative
- Generally gaining power throughout
- Some builds fundamentally transform how you play (Brimstone, Epic Fetus, etc.)

**14. Persistence:** Unlocks
- New items, characters, challenges, endings unlocked through achievements
- No permanent stat upgrades

**15. Starting Variance:** Character-varied + Random-varied
- Each character has different starting items/stats
- Eden has random starting items/stats
- Tainted characters add another layer

**16. Run Identity:** Emergent
- Builds emerge from what you find; "I became a Guppy run" or "this became a tear build"

**17. Skill vs Build Ratio:** Knowledge-dominant + Balanced
- Knowing item interactions is crucial (what to take, what to avoid, what combos)
- Execution still matters for dodging and positioning

---

## Hades

**1. Choice Timing:** Distributed
- Boon choices after most rooms
- **Pacing:** Event-triggered (room clears) + Resource-gated (shops with obols, wells with keys)

**2. Distribution Timing:** Immediate
- Boons work as soon as selected

**3. Agency:** Curated + Influenced
- Pick 1 of 3 boons (Curated)
- Keepsakes guarantee which god appears first (Influenced)
- Some boons affect future offerings (Influenced)

**4. Negative Acquisition:** Optional
- Chaos gates cost HP upfront for temporary debuff, then permanent buff
- No forced negatives in normal play

**5. Scarcity:** Moderate to Abundant
- Regular boon offerings, but can't take everything
- Enough gold to buy most shop items if you find shops

**6. Reversibility:** Permanent + Sellable
- Boons stay for the run
- Can sell boons at Wells of Charon
- **Commitment Weight:** Medium — permanent but frequent opportunities, selling is possible

**7. Capacity:** Unlimited + Contextual
- Can stack many boons
- Limited Cast slots (starts at 1, can increase)
- One Call at a time

**8. Interaction:** Synergistic
- Duo boons require specific prerequisites
- Legendary boons require specific god boons
- Status curse combos (e.g., Privileged Status)

**9. Upgrade Depth:** Linear + Evolutionary
- Boons can be upgraded with Poms of Power
- Duo and Legendary boons transform builds

**10. Power Source Diversity:** Multi-source
- Boons, Daedalus Hammers (weapon upgrades), Keepsakes, Mirror of Night (meta), Weapon Aspects

**11. Visibility:** Forecast + Present
- Door symbols preview reward type and which god
- See boon options when they appear

**12. Comprehension:** Transparent
- Boon descriptions clearly explain effects
- Numbers are visible

**13. Growth Pattern:** Additive

**14. Persistence:** Unlocks + Upgrades
- Unlock weapons, aspects, keepsakes (Unlocks)
- Mirror of Night provides permanent stat increases (Upgrades)

**15. Starting Variance:** Loadout-varied
- Choose weapon, aspect, and keepsake before each run
- Significantly affects playstyle

**16. Run Identity:** Emergent + Influenced
- Builds emerge from god offerings
- Keepsake choice influences early direction but doesn't guarantee anything

**17. Skill vs Build Ratio:** Balanced
- Combat execution matters (dodging, timing)
- Build matters (synergies, boon choices)
- Both contribute meaningfully to success

---

## Dead Cells

**1. Choice Timing:** Distributed + Pre-run
- Weapon/gear drops throughout
- Mutations selected at start of each biome
- **Pacing:** Event-triggered (room drops, challenge rooms) + Resource-gated (shops)

**2. Distribution Timing:** Immediate

**3. Agency:** Serendipitous + Curated
- Weapon drops are mostly random (Serendipitous)
- Mutations are chosen (Curated)
- Shops offer choices (Curated)

**4. Negative Acquisition:** Optional + Forced (higher difficulties)
- Cursed chests (Optional)
- Malaise in higher Boss Cells (Forced)

**5. Scarcity:** Abundant
- Lots of gear drops; main constraint is deciding what to keep

**6. Reversibility:** Swappable + Permanent
- 2 weapon slots, can swap anytime (Swappable)
- Mutations are locked until next biome (Permanent within biome)
- **Commitment Weight:** Light (weapons) to Medium (mutations)

**7. Capacity:** Hard cap
- 2 weapons, 2 skills, limited mutation slots (increases with BSC)

**8. Interaction:** Synergistic
- Affixes synergize (bleed, poison, burning)
- Mutations combo with weapon types (Brutality/Tactics/Survival)

**9. Upgrade Depth:** Linear (meta) + Flat (within run)
- Forge upgrades permanently improve gear quality (meta)
- Within a run, gear is what you find

**10. Power Source Diversity:** Multi-source
- Weapons, skills, mutations, scrolls (stat points), outfits (minor effects)

**11. Visibility:** Present + Forecast
- See current options
- Biome choice visible at transitions

**12. Comprehension:** Transparent
- Clear weapon/mutation descriptions

**13. Growth Pattern:** Additive

**14. Persistence:** Unlocks + Upgrades
- Unlock weapons, mutations, outfits, runes (permanent movement abilities)
- Forge upgrades persist

**15. Starting Variance:** Loadout-varied + Character-varied
- Choose starting gear
- DLC adds different characters with unique mechanics

**16. Run Identity:** Emergent + Influenced
- Build emerges from what you find
- Starting loadout and mutation path influence direction

**17. Skill vs Build Ratio:** Balanced to Execution-dominant
- Combat execution is demanding (parrying, dodging, timing)
- Build matters but won't carry you if you can't play

---

## Enter the Gungeon

**1. Choice Timing:** Distributed + Reactive
- Choices throughout, often reacting to what drops
- **Pacing:** Event-triggered (room clears, boss drops) + Resource-gated (shops)

**2. Distribution Timing:** Immediate

**3. Agency:** Serendipitous + Curated
- Chest drops are random (Serendipitous)
- Shops offer choices (Curated)

**4. Negative Acquisition:** Optional
- Cursed items exist but are optional
- Some shrines have risks

**5. Scarcity:** Moderate
- Limited keys (can't open every chest)
- Limited money
- Keys create genuine tension about which chests to open

**6. Reversibility:** Permanent + Swappable (rarely useful)
- Items are permanent
- Can technically drop guns but rarely want to
- **Commitment Weight:** Medium

**7. Capacity:** Unlimited (guns) + Contextual (active items)
- Can carry many guns (but ammo is a concern)
- 1 active item at a time (2 with backpack)

**8. Interaction:** Synergistic
- Gun/item synergies are explicit (shown in Ammonomicon)
- Certain item combinations create new effects

**9. Upgrade Depth:** Flat
- Items are at full power when acquired

**10. Power Source Diversity:** Multi-source
- Guns, passive items, active items

**11. Visibility:** Present

**12. Comprehension:** Learnable
- Many items to learn
- Synergies discoverable through play or external resources

**13. Growth Pattern:** Additive

**14. Persistence:** Unlocks
- Guns, items, characters, shortcuts
- No permanent power upgrades

**15. Starting Variance:** Character-varied
- Each Gungeoneer has unique starting loadout and passive ability

**16. Run Identity:** Emergent
- Builds emerge from drops

**17. Skill vs Build Ratio:** Balanced to Execution-dominant
- Dodge-rolling and shooting skill matter enormously
- Build helps but can't replace skill
- Boss fights especially test execution

---

## Noita

**1. Choice Timing:** Reactive
- Find wands and spells, then decide how to configure them
- **Pacing:** Event-triggered (exploration, Holy Mountain between zones)

**2. Distribution Timing:** Immediate

**3. Agency:** Serendipitous + Deterministic
- What wands/spells you find is random (Serendipitous)
- How you build wands is entirely player-controlled (Deterministic)

**4. Negative Acquisition:** Coupled + Optional
- Some perks have significant downsides (Coupled)
- Can choose to skip risky perks (Optional)

**5. Scarcity:** Moderate to Scarce
- Good wands/spells can be hard to find
- Holy Mountains are limited

**6. Reversibility:** Highly Swappable + Permanent
- Wands can be completely rebuilt at any time (Swappable)
- Perks are permanent
- **Commitment Weight:** Light (wands) to Heavy (perks)

**7. Capacity:** Hard cap
- 4 wand slots
- Limited spell slots per wand (varies by wand)

**8. Interaction:** Systemic
- Spells combine in emergent, complex ways
- Physics interactions with environment, liquids, materials
- Emergent chaos is the core appeal

**9. Upgrade Depth:** Transformative
- Wand building transforms base spells into entirely different behaviors
- Trigger spells, modifiers, etc. create new effects

**10. Power Source Diversity:** Multi-source
- Wands, spells, perks, flasks/potions, world interactions (kicking, throwing, physics)

**11. Visibility:** Present + Obscured
- See current options
- Many secrets, hidden spells, obscure interactions

**12. Comprehension:** Opaque + Learnable
- Wand mechanics (cast delay, recharge, mana drain) are complex and not fully explained in-game
- Can learn over time but wiki is almost required

**13. Growth Pattern:** Additive + Transformative
- Generally gaining power
- "God wands" can transform the game completely

**14. Persistence:** Unlocks (minimal)
- Some spells/perks unlock through achievements
- Much less meta-progression than other roguelites

**15. Starting Variance:** Minimal + Random-varied
- Always start in same place with same base equipment
- Starting wands have slight variance

**16. Run Identity:** Emergent
- Heavily dependent on what wands/spells you find
- A good wand changes everything

**17. Skill vs Build Ratio:** Knowledge-dominant + Balanced
- Understanding wand mechanics is crucial
- Execution matters for dodging in a physics-based environment
- Knowing secrets/tricks provides huge advantages

---

## Nuclear Throne

**1. Choice Timing:** Distributed
- Mutations after each level
- **Pacing:** Fixed interval (level completion triggers mutation choice)

**2. Distribution Timing:** Immediate

**3. Agency:** Curated + Serendipitous
- Choose 1 of 4 mutations (Curated)
- Weapon drops are random (Serendipitous)

**4. Negative Acquisition:** None
- Mutations are pure positives
- Some characters have built-in trade-offs (e.g., Melting has low HP)

**5. Scarcity:** Moderate
- Weapons drop frequently but can only carry 2
- Ammo can be scarce for certain weapon types

**6. Reversibility:** Permanent + Swappable
- Mutations are permanent
- 2 weapon slots, can swap by picking up new weapons
- **Commitment Weight:** Medium

**7. Capacity:** Hard cap
- 2 weapons
- Mutations soft cap around 9-10 (depending on ultra mutations)

**8. Interaction:** Synergistic
- Mutations combo with weapon types (e.g., Bolt Marrow with bolt weapons)
- Character abilities synergize with certain builds

**9. Upgrade Depth:** Flat
- Mutations are at full power when selected

**10. Power Source Diversity:** Dual source + Character abilities
- Weapons, mutations
- Character unique abilities (actives and passives)

**11. Visibility:** Present

**12. Comprehension:** Transparent
- Mutation descriptions are clear
- Weapon behavior is learnable through use

**13. Growth Pattern:** Additive

**14. Persistence:** Unlocks
- Characters, golden weapons (starting weapons), crowns (modifiers)
- No permanent power upgrades

**15. Starting Variance:** Character-varied
- Each character plays very differently (Fish can roll, Eyes can telekinesis, Crystal can shield, etc.)

**16. Run Identity:** Emergent + Influenced by character
- Build emerges from mutations and weapon finds
- Character choice influences what works

**17. Skill vs Build Ratio:** Execution-dominant
- Extremely twitchy, fast-paced shooter
- Reflexes and movement matter most
- Build helps but won't save poor execution

---

## Vampire Survivors

**1. Choice Timing:** Distributed
- Level-up choices throughout
- **Pacing:** Fixed interval (XP-based level-ups, very frequent early, slows down later)

**2. Distribution Timing:** Immediate

**3. Agency:** Curated
- Choose 1 of 3-4 options per level-up

**4. Negative Acquisition:** None
- Pure power gain

**5. Scarcity:** Abundant
- Constant stream of level-ups
- More options than you can take

**6. Reversibility:** Permanent + Evolutionary
- Choices are permanent
- Weapons evolve with correct passive item
- **Commitment Weight:** Medium (permanent but frequent choices)

**7. Capacity:** Hard cap
- 6 weapon slots
- 6 passive item slots

**8. Interaction:** Synergistic
- Evolution requirements (specific weapon + specific passive)
- Passives affect weapons (e.g., Spinach affects all damage)

**9. Upgrade Depth:** Linear + Evolutionary
- Weapons level up incrementally (8 levels)
- Final evolution transforms weapon

**10. Power Source Diversity:** Single source + Character
- Primarily just the upgrade system
- Character choice adds starting weapon/passive

**11. Visibility:** Present

**12. Comprehension:** Transparent
- Clear what everything does

**13. Growth Pattern:** Additive (exponential in practice)
- Power snowballs dramatically

**14. Persistence:** Unlocks + Upgrades
- Unlock characters, stages, weapons (Unlocks)
- PowerUps provide permanent stat boosts (Upgrades)

**15. Starting Variance:** Character-varied + Loadout-varied
- Different characters have different starting weapons and stats
- Some characters let you choose starting weapon

**16. Run Identity:** Early-crystallizing
- First few weapon choices largely define the run
- Hard to pivot once committed

**17. Skill vs Build Ratio:** Build-dominant
- Right build plays itself
- Positioning matters but is secondary
- Some execution in dodging gaps, but mostly automatic

---

## Brotato

**1. Choice Timing:** Distributed
- Shop between waves
- **Pacing:** Fixed interval (wave completion)

**2. Distribution Timing:** Immediate

**3. Agency:** Curated + Influenced
- Shop offers random items, you choose what to buy (Curated)
- Can reroll shop (Influenced)

**4. Negative Acquisition:** Optional + Character-based
- Some items have stat penalties (Optional)
- Some characters have built-in negatives (e.g., can't move, limited slots)

**5. Scarcity:** Moderate
- Limited gold per wave
- Must prioritize purchases

**6. Reversibility:** Swappable + Permanent
- Weapons can be sold (recover some gold)
- Stats from items are permanent for the run
- **Commitment Weight:** Light to Medium

**7. Capacity:** Hard cap
- 6 weapon slots
- Some characters modify this

**8. Interaction:** Synergistic
- Stats scale together (e.g., crit + crit damage)
- Weapon types benefit from specific stats

**9. Upgrade Depth:** Linear
- Weapons can be upgraded/tiered up in shop

**10. Power Source Diversity:** Dual source
- Weapons, items (which give stats)

**11. Visibility:** Complete
- See entire shop
- Know what items exist

**12. Comprehension:** Transparent
- Clear stat effects

**13. Growth Pattern:** Additive

**14. Persistence:** Unlocks
- Characters, items, weapons

**15. Starting Variance:** Character-varied
- Each character has unique restrictions/bonuses
- Wide variety of playstyles (melee only, ranged only, one weapon, etc.)

**16. Run Identity:** Emergent + Influenced by character
- Build emerges from shop offerings
- Character choice heavily constrains options

**17. Skill vs Build Ratio:** Build-dominant + some Execution
- Build matters most
- Movement and positioning help but aren't primary

---

## SNKRX

**1. Choice Timing:** Distributed
- Shop between rounds
- **Pacing:** Fixed interval (round completion)

**2. Distribution Timing:** Immediate

**3. Agency:** Curated + Influenced
- Shop offers random units (Curated)
- Can reroll (Influenced)
- Later rounds unlock higher tier units

**4. Negative Acquisition:** None

**5. Scarcity:** Moderate
- Limited gold per round

**6. Reversibility:** Sellable + Swappable
- Can sell units
- Can rearrange snake order
- **Commitment Weight:** Light

**7. Capacity:** Hard cap
- Snake length limit (increases as you progress)

**8. Interaction:** Synergistic
- Class synergies (like auto-battlers)
- Units trigger off each other

**9. Upgrade Depth:** Linear
- Units upgrade by buying duplicates (3 to level up, like auto-battlers)

**10. Power Source Diversity:** Single source
- Just units with class bonuses

**11. Visibility:** Complete + Pool-visible
- See shop
- Know what units exist per tier

**12. Comprehension:** Transparent
- Clear ability descriptions

**13. Growth Pattern:** Additive

**14. Persistence:** Unlocks
- Units, classes

**15. Starting Variance:** Character-varied
- Different starting "leader" units with different passives
- *(Note: I'm less certain on this, may need verification)*

**16. Run Identity:** Emergent
- Based on what synergies you find/can build

**17. Skill vs Build Ratio:** Build-dominant + some Execution
- Auto-battler core (build matters most)
- Snake movement requires some skill/attention

---

## 20 Minutes Till Dawn

**1. Choice Timing:** Distributed
- Level-up choices throughout
- **Pacing:** Fixed interval (XP-based, frequent)

**2. Distribution Timing:** Immediate

**3. Agency:** Curated
- Choose 1 of 3-4 options

**4. Negative Acquisition:** None (or minimal)

**5. Scarcity:** Abundant
- Frequent level-ups

**6. Reversibility:** Permanent
- **Commitment Weight:** Medium

**7. Capacity:** Soft cap
- Many upgrade slots, but some upgrades max out

**8. Interaction:** Synergistic
- Upgrade combos (summons, bullets, elemental effects)

**9. Upgrade Depth:** Linear
- Upgrades can level up

**10. Power Source Diversity:** Dual source
- Weapon choice (selected at start) + upgrades

**11. Visibility:** Present

**12. Comprehension:** Transparent

**13. Growth Pattern:** Additive

**14. Persistence:** Unlocks
- Characters, weapons

**15. Starting Variance:** Character-varied + Loadout-varied
- Different characters have different abilities
- Weapon choice at start affects available upgrades

**16. Run Identity:** Emergent + Influenced by starting weapon
- Weapon choice matters (e.g., shotgun vs sniper build around different upgrades)

**17. Skill vs Build Ratio:** Balanced
- More aiming skill required than Vampire Survivors
- Build still matters
