## Experimental Game 13: The Auction House

*A roguelite where your build is purchased in competitive pre-run auctions against ghost bidders.*

**Core Fantasy:** You're a treasure hunter attending underground auctions before each expedition. The best items go to the highest bidder, but overspending leaves you under-equipped for the actual run.

### Acquisition Source: Hybrid
Each auction presents a curated selection of 8-12 items, but the selection itself is randomly generated from a large pool. You see exactly what's available and can plan your bidding strategy. However, you're competing against AI "ghost bidders" whose behavior has randomized preferences—sometimes they desperately want the item you need, sometimes they don't care. This creates a hybrid where you have full information about items but uncertainty about competition.

### Acquisition Timing: Frontloaded
Everything happens before the run begins. You enter the dungeon with exactly what you won at auction—no shops, no drops, no mid-run additions. The entire "build-making" phase is compressed into a frantic bidding war. Once the gavel falls on the last item, your loadout is locked.

### Resource Scarcity: Drought/Feast
Auction quality varies wildly between runs. Sometimes the lot includes three legendary weapons and rare synergy pieces—a feast where bidding wars drive prices to absurd heights. Sometimes it's garbage—a drought where you're fighting over scraps and trying to assemble something functional from mediocre pieces. Learning to build effectively during droughts separates good players from great ones.

### Resource Conversion: Traded
Gold doesn't disappear when spent—it goes to the auction house (metaphorically to other bidders). This creates interesting dynamics: letting someone else win an item means they have less gold for the next item. You can "pump" prices on items you don't want to drain opponents' resources before the item you actually need comes up. It's a zero-sum economy where reading the room matters as much as valuing items.

### Choice Timing: Immediate with Auction Pacing
Bids must be placed immediately when items come up—no time to deliberate. The auction moves fast, forcing gut decisions. However, you can see the remaining items in the lot, so there's strategic "passing" on early items to save gold for later ones.

**Pacing Subtable: Event-Driven**
The auction itself is the pacing mechanism. Items appear one at a time, each a decision point. The dungeon run afterward is almost a formality—the real game was the auction.

### Commitment Weight: Critical
**Subtable: Critical**
Won an item? It's yours. Spent your gold? It's gone. There's no "undo" in an auction. Every bid is a commitment that reshapes what's possible for the rest of the auction. Overbidding on an early item can leave you unable to compete for the perfect synergy piece that appears later.

### Reversibility: Permanent
Items won are permanently part of your loadout for this run. You can't sell back, can't trade with other bidders, can't change your mind. The auction creates your build in one irreversible sequence of decisions.

### Persistence: Unlocks
Between runs, you unlock new items that can appear in future auctions and new ghost bidder personalities that change auction dynamics. You might unlock a "collector" ghost who overbids on matching sets, or a "sniper" who waits until the last second. Meta-progression expands both what you can buy and who you're buying against.

### Power Relationship: Dependent
Your power is entirely dependent on auction outcomes. Bad auction? Weak run. The dungeon difficulty doesn't scale to what you purchased—it's fixed. This means some runs are doomed from the auction floor, but it also means skilled bidding translates directly to easier runs.

### Element Interaction: Synergistic
Items are designed with clear synergies: poison weapons + poison amplifiers, crit gear + crit multipliers. The auction becomes a puzzle of "what synergies can I assemble from this lot?" Sometimes the strongest build isn't the most expensive items—it's the cheap pieces that happen to combo.

### Competition Type: Competitive (Async)
Ghost bidders are recordings of real player auction behavior from past runs. You're competing against actual human strategies, just time-shifted. Leaderboards track auction efficiency (dungeon performance relative to gold spent), creating a metagame around bidding strategy.

### Progression Structure: Linear
The dungeon itself is straightforward—a gauntlet of encounters. All the interesting decisions happened at auction. The run is where you discover whether your purchases were wise.

### Information Transparency: Transparent
You see all items, all ghost bidder gold totals, and item synergies are clearly labeled. No hidden information—the skill is in reading ghost behavior patterns and valuing items correctly under time pressure.

### Feedback Loop: Delayed
You don't know if your auction strategy was correct until you're in the dungeon. That poison build seemed clever, but now you're facing poison-immune enemies. The feedback on your bidding decisions comes through gameplay consequences.

### Difficulty Arc: Variable
Entirely depends on auction outcomes. Feast auctions where you assembled a god-build lead to easy runs. Drought auctions with desperate compromises lead to brutal difficulty. The variance is the point.

### Completion State: Victory
Each run is win/lose. Complete the dungeon with your auctioned loadout or die trying. The goal is consistent victory through auction mastery.

### Randomness Role: High
Auction contents, ghost bidder preferences, enemy compositions—all heavily randomized. But within that randomness, skill in bidding and building creates consistent edges.

---

## Experimental Game 14: The Bloodline Labyrinth

*A roguelite where the skill tree IS your family tree—ancestors' choices determine your starting position, and your choices become your descendants' inheritance.*

**Core Fantasy:** You're the latest heir of a dungeon-delving dynasty. The family skill tree has been carved over generations—some branches flourishing, others stunted. Your run begins where your ancestors left off, and ends by choosing which branch of the family continues.

### Acquisition Source: Curated by Ancestry
Available skills are determined by your lineage. If your great-grandmother specialized in fire magic, that branch is well-developed and offers advanced fire options. If no ancestor touched necromancy, that branch barely exists. You choose from what your bloodline has cultivated, creating a curated selection that evolved over many generations.

### Acquisition Timing: Distributed with Inheritance Boost
You inherit some skills at run start (the "ancestral talents" your parent mastered), then acquire more during the run. Early game is shaped by inheritance; late game is shaped by your own choices. Your starting power reflects generational investment.

### Resource Scarcity: Abundant (Generationally Earned)
Within a single run, skill points feel abundant—your ancestors' sacrifices created wealth. But this abundance was built through generations of scarcity. The family tree represents centuries of careful investment. Squandering it on bad builds wastes ancestral effort.

### Resource Conversion: Invested
Skill points invested in a branch grow over generations. A branch with three generations of investment offers stronger versions of skills than a freshly-opened branch. Your choices don't just affect this run—they're investments in your descendants' power. Taking a suboptimal skill now might create optimal options later.

### Choice Timing: Distributed with Inheritance Phase
Run start: choose which ancestor to descend from (each offers different inherited skills). Mid-run: develop your own branch. Run end: choose which of your skills become "mastered" and pass to descendants with bonuses.

**Pacing Subtable: Milestone-Based**
Major family decisions happen at generation transitions. Within a run, skill acquisition follows milestone pacing (boss kills, area completions). But the big decisions—which bloodline to continue, which skills to master—happen between generations.

### Commitment Weight: Critical (Generational)
**Subtable: Critical**
Skills mastered at death become permanent additions to the family tree. Choosing wrong doesn't just hurt this run—it shapes the family for generations. A bad mastery choice might create a dead-end branch that future heirs must work around.

### Reversibility: Permanent (Generationally)
Individual run choices are permanent, but more importantly, generational choices are permanent. You can't un-master a skill, can't prune the family tree. Bad ancestors create permanent complications. The only way forward is to build around mistakes.

### Persistence: Inherited
This is the core mechanic. Everything persists through inheritance. The family tree is the save file, growing and branching with each generation. Progress isn't measured in unlocks but in how developed your bloodline has become.

### Power Relationship: Scaling (Generational)
Power scales with generational investment. A hundred-generation bloodline starts runs massively more powerful than a new family. But they also have more "weight"—more ancestral choices constraining current options. Fresh bloodlines have freedom but weakness.

### Element Interaction: Hierarchical
Skills exist in family branches with clear hierarchies. You must have the parent skill to access the child. Deep investment in one branch creates specialists; broad shallow investment creates generalists. The tree structure enforces this hierarchy.

### Competition Type: Solo with Legacy
Each player has their own family tree. No competition, but legacy matters—your bloodline is judged by how deep and developed it becomes. Bragging rights come from centuries-old dynasties with intricate, optimized trees.

### Progression Structure: Branching (Literally)
The skill tree IS a branching structure. Each generation adds branches or deepens existing ones. The progression structure is the core mechanic made literal—you navigate a tree that you and your ancestors built.

### Information Transparency: Transparent
The family tree is fully visible. You can see exactly what each ancestor chose, what's well-developed, what's neglected. Planning which branches to develop is possible because all information is available.

### Feedback Loop: Generational (Very Delayed)
You won't know if a mastery choice was correct until descendants try to use it. This creates extremely delayed feedback—sometimes three or four generations pass before you realize an ancestral mistake. But this also creates emergent stories: "This run failed because great-great-grandmother wasted mastery on that useless skill."

### Difficulty Arc: Variable by Lineage
Difficulty depends heavily on which bloodline you choose to continue. Well-developed ancestral lines make early runs easier. New branches being explored are harder. You can choose your difficulty by choosing your ancestors.

### Completion State: Progress (Generational)
No single run "wins" in a traditional sense. The goal is generational progress—developing the family tree, creating powerful bloodlines, building a dynasty. Individual runs are chapters in a longer story.

### Randomness Role: Low
Randomness affects dungeon layouts and enemy spawns, but the build side—the family tree—is entirely deterministic. Your bloodline is exactly what you and your ancestors made it. This creates a seeded-like experience where builds are reproducible through lineage choice.

---

## Experimental Game 15: The Expedition Toolkit

*A roguelite where you pack limited-use tools before departure, manage their wear during the expedition, and swap between them tactically in combat.*

**Core Fantasy:** You're an explorer preparing for a dangerous expedition. Your toolkit is your build—each tool has limited durability, and running out mid-expedition is disastrous. Strategic tool use and careful packing determine survival.

### Acquisition Source: Curated by Inventory
Before departure, you pack from your workshop's inventory—a curated selection you've built up over many expeditions. You choose exactly which tools to bring, but inventory space is limited. The selection is yours; the constraint is capacity.

### Acquisition Timing: Frontloaded with Rare Finds
Almost everything is packed pre-expedition. Occasionally you find tool caches during exploration (hidden workshops, abandoned campsites), but these are rare bonuses, not the core progression. Your build is what you packed.

### Resource Scarcity: Scarce (Durability)
Tools have limited uses. Your best pickaxe might only have 20 swings. Your most powerful weapon might only last 50 strikes. Scarcity isn't about acquiring tools—it's about using them wisely. Every swing counts.

### Resource Conversion: Spent (Durability as Resource)
Using tools spends their durability. There's no recovery, no repair mid-expedition. Each use is permanent resource expenditure. The conversion is tool-use → durability-loss → eventual tool-break.

### Resource Conversion Extended: Invested (Workshop)
Between expeditions, you invest resources into your workshop, creating new tools for future expeditions. This is the "real" resource conversion—expedition salvage becomes workshop upgrades becomes better tools.

### Choice Timing: Pre-run with Tactical Swapping
Tool selection is pre-run (packing phase). Tool usage is immediate (mid-combat swapping). You decide what to bring before knowing exactly what you'll face; you decide when to use each tool in real-time tactical situations.

**Pacing Subtable: Mixed**
Packing is deliberate and untimed. Expedition exploration is self-paced. Combat requires immediate tactical decisions about tool swapping. Multiple pacing modes for different phases.

### Commitment Weight: High (Packing) + Critical (Usage)
**Subtable: High for packing, Critical for usage**
Packing decisions are important but you can redistribute during the packing phase. Once packed and departed, critically committed. Using a tool's last durability is irreversible—that tool is gone for this expedition.

### Reversibility: Permanent (Per-Expedition)
Used durability doesn't return. Broken tools stay broken until you return to workshop. Within an expedition, all tool-use is permanent expenditure.

### Persistence: Unlocks + Investment
Workshop upgrades persist. Tool blueprints unlock permanently. But individual tools must be crafted each time—you don't keep expedition tools, you keep the ability to make them. Meta-progression expands your potential toolkit, not your actual tools.

### Power Relationship: Dependent on Packing
Expedition power is entirely dependent on what you packed. No drops, no shops, no scaling. Brought the wrong tools? Expedition fails. This creates strong pressure to pack correctly and explore workshop options.

### Element Interaction: Synergistic (Tool Combos)
Tools synergize: the lantern reveals weak points, the hammer exploits them. The rope reaches high places, the grappling hook makes them accessible. Tool combos are designed and intended—using tools together is more powerful than using them separately.

### Competition Type: Solo
Personal expeditions. No multiplayer, no competition. Just you, your toolkit, and the expedition.

### Progression Structure: Linear (Expedition) + Branching (Workshop)
Each expedition is linear—explore deeper into the unknown. But workshop development branches—specialize in mining tools, combat tools, exploration tools, etc. Your "build" across many expeditions is which workshop branches you've developed.

### Information Transparency: Partially Hidden
You know what's in your toolkit (transparent). You don't know exactly what challenges the expedition holds (hidden). Packing requires educated guesses about what you'll need.

### Feedback Loop: Immediate (Tool Use) + Delayed (Packing)
Using a tool gives immediate feedback—it worked or didn't. But whether you packed correctly isn't clear until mid-expedition when you need something you didn't bring. The packing feedback is delayed.

### Difficulty Arc: Escalating (Expedition Depth)
Deeper exploration means harder challenges. Early areas are forgiving; deep areas demand well-packed toolkits. Difficulty escalates with expedition progress.

### Completion State: Victory + Progress
Each expedition has victory conditions (reach the goal, retrieve the artifact). But there's also progress—workshop development, blueprint collection. You can "lose" an expedition but still progress if you recovered salvage.

### Randomness Role: Low (Packing) + High (Expedition)
You control your toolkit (low randomness). The expedition challenges you face are randomized (high randomness). The skill is packing for unknown situations.

---

## Experimental Game 16: Wave Architect

*A roguelite where you control when power waves hit, and each wave opens different build branches—timing your waves determines your entire build path.*

**Core Fantasy:** You're a surfer of magical tides. Power comes in waves that you summon at will, but each wave transforms available options. Timing your wave-riding determines what builds are even possible.

### Acquisition Source: Wave-Generated
Skills/items don't drop from enemies or appear in shops. They crystallize from power waves. When you trigger a wave, it generates a specific selection of options based on wave timing, type, and your current state. The wave IS the acquisition source.

### Acquisition Timing: Player-Controlled
You control when waves hit. Trigger waves early for early-game options. Save wave charges for late-game power spikes. The timing is entirely in your hands, but wave charges are limited—you can't simply spam waves.

### Resource Scarcity: Drought/Feast (Wave Cycles)
Between waves: drought. No new power, no new options. During waves: feast. Abundant choices crystallize rapidly. Managing drought phases (conserving resources, surviving) while planning for feast phases (which waves to trigger when) is the core loop.

### Resource Conversion: Invested (Wave Energy)
Surviving encounters builds wave energy. This energy is invested into triggering waves. Bigger energy investments trigger more powerful waves with better options. It's not spent (you don't lose energy when hit), it's invested (energy determines wave quality).

### Choice Timing: Delayed + Player-Controlled
You don't choose immediately when options appear. Waves crystalize options that float until you claim them or the wave ends. During a wave, you're frantically grabbing options while fighting. After the wave, options dissolve. Timing is everything.

**Pacing Subtable: Player-Controlled**
You decide when waves happen. Self-paced exploration between waves, frantic activity during waves. The game's tempo is in your hands.

### Commitment Weight: High (Wave Triggers)
**Subtable: High**
Triggering a wave is a significant commitment—you only have limited charges per run. But within a wave, grabbing options is quick and reversible (until the wave ends). The macro decision (when to wave) is high commitment; micro decisions (what to grab) are lower commitment.

### Reversibility: Fluid (During Waves) + Permanent (After)
During a wave, you can swap and change claimed options freely. When the wave ends, everything locks in permanently. This creates frantic optimization windows followed by permanent consequences.

### Persistence: Unlocks
Meta-progression unlocks new wave types (fire waves, ice waves, chaos waves) that generate different option pools. Also unlocks wave modifiers that change wave behavior. Your "meta-build" is which wave types you prefer.

### Power Relationship: Dependent on Waves
No waves, no power progression. Your strength is entirely dependent on successful wave-riding. Skip waves, stay weak. This creates pressure to engage with the wave system rather than avoiding it.

### Element Interaction: Hierarchical (Wave-Locked)
Each wave type has hierarchies. Fire waves unlock fire options; advanced fire requires multiple fire waves. The wave you're in determines what hierarchy tier is accessible. Cross-wave synergies exist but require careful wave ordering.

### Competition Type: Solo
Personal wave-riding. The challenge is mastering wave timing against the game, not against other players.

### Progression Structure: Branching (Wave-Determined)
Your build path branches based on wave choices. Fire wave early → fire build available. Ice wave early → ice build available. Each wave opens branches and closes others (wave charges are limited). The branching structure is carved by your wave decisions.

### Information Transparency: Transparent (Wave Preview)
Before triggering a wave, you see what option categories it will generate (not exact options, but types). You can plan wave order by previewing wave contents. Information is available for planning.

### Feedback Loop: Immediate (Wave Quality)
Wave quality is immediately apparent—you see what crystallized. Whether that was a good wave is immediately clear. Long-term feedback (was this wave ORDER correct) is more delayed.

### Difficulty Arc: Variable (Wave-Controlled)
Triggering waves increases your power. Not triggering waves keeps difficulty high. You control your own difficulty curve through wave timing. Aggressive early waves = easier early game. Saved waves = harder early, explosive late.

### Completion State: Victory
Complete the run by reaching the end with whatever build your waves created. Traditional roguelite victory condition.

### Randomness Role: Seeded (Wave Contents)
Each wave has predetermined contents based on its type and your current state. Same wave triggered at same time generates same options. There's randomness in enemy encounters, but wave contents are deterministic. Optimal wave orders can be solved.

---

## Experimental Game 17: The Gambler's Dungeon

*A roguelite where you place bets on your own performance before each run, and your bets determine what resources and options are available.*

**Core Fantasy:** You're a gambler who bets on yourself. Before entering the dungeon, you wager at the betting house. Bet on killing 50 enemies? You start with bonus damage but lose everything if you fail. Your bets shape your build, and your build must fulfill your bets.

### Acquisition Source: Bet-Generated
Items and skills aren't found—they're collateral. When you place a bet, the house provides "stakes" equipment related to that bet. Bet on speedrunning? You get speed equipment. Bet on kill count? You get damage equipment. Your bets generate your options.

### Acquisition Timing: Frontloaded (Betting Phase)
All bets are placed before the run. All equipment is received before entry. No mid-run betting, no new equipment. Your build is your bets made manifest.

### Resource Scarcity: Self-Imposed
Conservative bets give modest equipment—scarcity. Aggressive bets give powerful equipment—abundance. But abundance comes with harder win conditions. You choose your scarcity level through bet ambition.

### Resource Conversion: Traded (Risk ↔ Reward)
You trade safety for power. Each bet increases your potential rewards but also your potential loss. The currency is risk—spending risk (accepting harder conditions) to buy power (better equipment). It's a direct trade.

### Choice Timing: Frontloaded + Immediate (Performance)
Bets are frontloaded. But fulfilling bets requires immediate decisions during the run. That "kill 50 enemies" bet requires constant attention to kill count. Bet timing is pre-run; performance timing is immediate.

**Pacing Subtable: Event-Driven (Bet Resolution)**
The run is punctuated by bet checkpoints. "Kill 10 enemies by Room 3" creates event-driven pacing where specific moments must deliver results. Bets structure the run's tempo.

### Commitment Weight: Critical
**Subtable: Critical**
Bets cannot be canceled. Equipment cannot be returned. Fail a bet and lose everything (run ends in debt, lose meta-progress). The weight is as critical as it gets—you're gambling your progress.

### Reversibility: Permanent
Once bet, cannot be unbet. Once equipment received, cannot be returned. Once failed, cannot be unfailed. Everything is permanent and consequential.

### Persistence: Unlocks + Wagered
Successful bets unlock new bet types and betting house upgrades. But there's also a "bank" of winnings that can be wagered on future runs. Meta-progress can be gambled—bet your unlocks for bigger rewards, lose them if you fail.

### Power Relationship: Dependent on Bets
Power comes entirely from bet-provided equipment. Timid bets = weak equipment = hard run. Ambitious bets = strong equipment = must meet conditions. Power depends on betting courage.

### Element Interaction: Synergistic (Bet Combos)
Certain bets synergize: "kill quickly" + "take no damage" provide equipment that combos (glass cannon builds). The betting house offers "parlay" bets that combine conditions for multiplicative rewards. Building synergies through bet combinations is the skill.

### Competition Type: Competitive (Async Leaderboards)
Leaderboards track bet ambition and success rate. The most prestigious players consistently win aggressive bets. There's social pressure to bet big—conservative betting is looked down upon.

### Progression Structure: Linear (Run) + Branching (Bets)
The dungeon is linear. But bet options branch—specializing in speed bets unlocks deeper speed bet trees. Your betting "career" branches based on what you're good at.

### Information Transparency: Transparent
Bet conditions are fully disclosed. Equipment provided is fully visible. Win/lose conditions are clear. No hidden information—the gamble is in your execution, not in unknown rules.

### Feedback Loop: Immediate (Bet Tracking)
A UI tracks all active bets and your progress toward them. You always know exactly where you stand. Feedback on bet-fulfillment is constant and immediate.

### Difficulty Arc: Self-Determined
Conservative bets = consistent difficulty. Escalating bets = escalating difficulty. You choose your arc through bet patterns. Mastery means betting aggressively and still winning.

### Completion State: Victory (+ Winnings)
Victory means completing the dungeon AND fulfilling all bets. Completing the dungeon but failing bets is a loss. The completion state is compound—survive AND deliver.

### Randomness Role: Low
Dungeon layouts and enemies are somewhat random, but bet conditions are fixed. Your "build" (the bets you placed) is entirely deterministic. Winning comes from knowing your capabilities and betting accurately.

---

## Experimental Game 18: The Score

*A roguelite where you compose a "score" of abilities before each run, and they play out in the sequence you composed—timing and order create the build.*

**Core Fantasy:** You're a battle-composer. Before each run, you arrange abilities into a musical score. During the run, the score plays automatically—you control movement and targeting, but abilities activate in the sequence you composed. Your build is your composition.

### Acquisition Source: Curated (Personal Library)
You compose from your personal ability library—a curated collection built over many runs. Each ability is like an instrument. More abilities unlock through play, expanding compositional options.

### Acquisition Timing: Frontloaded (Composition Phase)
The entire score is written before the run. No improvisation, no mid-run changes. What you composed is what plays. The "acquisition" of your build is entirely frontloaded into the composition phase.

### Resource Scarcity: Constrained (Score Length)
Scores have limited measures. You can't compose everything—there isn't enough space. Scarcity is compositional space, not ability availability. Every measure you fill is one you can't use for something else.

### Resource Conversion: Invested (Measure Space)
Filling a measure invests that space. Powerful abilities take more measures. You invest limited space into specific effects. The conversion is space → ability → power.

### Choice Timing: Delayed (Pre-Run) + Automatic (In-Run)
Composition is delayed—you can revise until you start. But once started, choices become automatic. Abilities trigger on their beat whether you want them to or not. You're committed to your composition.

**Pacing Subtable: Fixed Tempo**
The score has a tempo—abilities trigger on beats. Faster tempos mean more ability triggers but less time between them. You set tempo during composition, creating fixed pacing you must play around.

### Commitment Weight: High (Composition) + Automatic (Execution)
**Subtable: High**
Composition is high commitment—significant decisions about what goes where. Execution is automatic—no commitment required because there are no choices. You've pre-committed to everything.

### Reversibility: Permanent (Once Started)
Pre-run composition is fluid and revisable. Once the run starts, the score is locked. Measures play in order, permanently and automatically. No revision, no improvisation.

### Persistence: Unlocks
New abilities unlock for future compositions. New tempos unlock. New score structures (bridges, codas, reprises) unlock. Meta-progression expands compositional vocabulary.

### Power Relationship: Dependent on Composition
Power is entirely composition-dependent. Well-composed score = powerful run. Bad composition = weak run. The game is won or lost in the composition phase.

### Element Interaction: Synergistic (Harmonic Combos)
Abilities synergize based on sequence. Ability A followed immediately by Ability B creates a "harmonic" bonus. Distant abilities create "resonance" if they rhyme. The score structure creates synergies through placement and timing.

### Competition Type: Competitive (Composition Sharing)
Players share compositions. Leaderboards track composition elegance (power relative to measures used). A culture of composition critique and improvement develops. Competition is about compositional skill.

### Progression Structure: Linear (Run) + Branching (Library)
Each run is linear—the score plays forward. But your ability library branches—instrumental families, schools of composition. Your meta-build is which compositional tradition you've developed.

### Information Transparency: Transparent
You see exactly what each ability does, how many measures it takes, what harmonics it creates with other abilities. Composition is fully informed. No hidden interactions.

### Feedback Loop: Immediate (Score Playback)
You can preview compositions before running. The actual run shows exactly what you composed playing out. Feedback is immediate—you see and hear your composition in action.

### Difficulty Arc: Escalating (Movements)
Runs have multiple "movements" (acts). Later movements have faster tempo and harder challenges. Your composition must work across all movements. Difficulty escalates with progression.

### Completion State: Victory + Elegance
Victory is completing the dungeon. But there's also an elegance rating—how efficiently your composition achieved victory. Mastery is winning with minimal, elegant compositions.

### Randomness Role: Low (Deterministic Playback)
Compositions play exactly as written. Enemy spawns have some randomness, but ability sequences are entirely deterministic. The same composition does the same thing every time. Skill is composing for variable situations.

---

## Experimental Game 19: The Cartographer's Gambit

*A roguelite where you must commit to exploration routes before the map is revealed, and your build emerges from what you discover along your chosen paths.*

**Core Fantasy:** You're a cartographer exploring unknown territories. Before setting out, you commit to a general exploration plan—will you head north first, or circle east? Your route determines what you find, and what you find becomes your build.

### Acquisition Source: Discovery-Based
Items and skills aren't purchased or dropped—they're discovered at specific map locations. Different regions hold different discoveries. Your route determines your discovery pool. The map IS your acquisition source.

### Acquisition Timing: Distributed (By Exploration)
Discoveries happen throughout the run as you explore. Early exploration = early discoveries. The timing is distributed according to your movement through the map.

### Resource Scarcity: Scarce (Coverage Limits)
You can't explore everywhere. Time/stamina limits force route choices. Not discovering something means you don't have it. Scarcity is coverage—you'll always leave regions unexplored, discoveries unfound.

### Resource Conversion: Invested (Exploration Time)
Time spent exploring a region is invested there. More time = more discoveries, but less time for other regions. You invest limited exploration capacity into specific areas.

### Choice Timing: Pre-Run (Route Planning) + Immediate (Navigation)
Route commitment is pre-run. But navigation within that route involves immediate choices—which branch of the planned path to take first, how to respond to discoveries.

**Pacing Subtable: Self-Paced with Constraints**
You control exploration speed, but stamina limits create time pressure. Self-paced in the moment, constrained overall. Pacing is about managing exploration urgency.

### Commitment Weight: Critical (Route) + High (Branch)
**Subtable: Critical for route, High for branch**
Your general route is critically committed pre-run. Branch choices within the route are high commitment but less severe. Abandoning your route entirely is possible but costly.

### Reversibility: Permanent (Distance Traveled)
Exploration spent is permanent. You can't unexplore a region. Discoveries found are permanent—you keep what you find. But discoveries missed are also permanent—no going back to previously skipped areas.

### Persistence: Unlocks (Cartography)
Successful explorations add regions to your persistent map. Future runs can plan routes through known regions (predictable discoveries) and unknown regions (gambles). Meta-progression is map completion.

### Power Relationship: Dependent on Route
Power depends entirely on what your route discovers. Lucky route into rich regions = powerful. Unlucky route into barren areas = weak. Route planning based on map knowledge reduces this dependency.

### Element Interaction: Geographic (Regional Synergies)
Adjacent regions share themes. Exploring a full region unlocks regional synergies. Scattered exploration across regions finds more variety but fewer synergies. Geographic clustering creates interaction patterns.

### Competition Type: Solo
Personal cartography. No competition—just you versus the unknown map.

### Progression Structure: Branching (Map Branches)
The map naturally branches. Your route choices determine which branches you explore. Progression is literally branching through geographic space.

### Information Transparency: Hidden → Revealed
The core mechanic. Map starts hidden. Exploration reveals it. Pre-run planning works with incomplete information. The transparency changes as you play.

### Feedback Loop: Delayed (Discovery Quality)
You don't know if your route was good until you see what you discover. Planning feedback is delayed—the value of route choices reveals over time.

### Difficulty Arc: Variable (Regional Difficulty)
Different regions have different difficulty. Your route determines your difficulty path. Expert cartographers plan routes through appropriate difficulty regions.

### Completion State: Progress (Map Coverage)
No single run "wins." Each run adds to total map coverage. The goal is complete cartography over many runs. Individual runs are expeditions contributing to larger understanding.

### Randomness Role: High (Undiscovered) + Low (Discovered)
Unexplored regions are random—you don't know what's there. But explored regions (on subsequent runs) are known. Randomness decreases as cartography progresses. Early game is gambling; late game is planning.

---

## Experimental Game 20: The Embassy

*A roguelite where you maintain alignments with multiple factions, can swap between faction stances mid-combat, and your pre-run diplomatic groundwork determines what stances are available.*

**Core Fantasy:** You're a diplomat navigating a war-torn realm. Multiple factions offer their power—but taking from one offends others. Before each mission, you conduct diplomacy. During the mission, you swap between faction alignments to access different powers.

### Acquisition Source: Faction-Provided
Powers come from faction alignment. Aligned with the Fire Kingdom? Access fire powers. Aligned with the Shadow Court? Access shadow powers. Factions are the sources; alignment unlocks access.

### Acquisition Timing: Distributed (Diplomatic Phases)
Pre-run diplomacy establishes baseline alignments. Mid-run actions shift alignments further. Both timing points matter. Your build evolves through ongoing diplomatic choices.

### Resource Scarcity: Zero-Sum (Faction Relations)
Gaining one faction's favor costs another's. Total faction approval is roughly fixed—you redistribute it between factions. Scarcity is relationship space, not power availability.

### Resource Conversion: Traded (Favor Trading)
You trade favor between factions. Help the Fire Kingdom to gain fire favor, lose shadow favor. It's literal trading—faction relationships are currency.

### Choice Timing: Pre-Run (Diplomacy) + Immediate (Stance Swapping)
Diplomatic negotiations are pre-run, deliberate affairs. Combat stance swapping is immediate and tactical. Two modes of choice timing for two modes of play.

**Pacing Subtable: Mixed**
Diplomacy phases are turn-based and thoughtful. Combat is real-time and frantic. Two pacing modes coexist.

### Commitment Weight: High (Diplomacy) + Low (Stances)
**Subtable: High for diplomacy, Low for stances**
Pre-run diplomatic concessions are significant—you're committing to faction relationships. But stance swapping mid-combat is fluid—you can change stances freely, no commitment.

### Reversibility: Fluid (Stances) + Difficult (Diplomacy)
Stances swap freely. But diplomatic damage takes runs to repair. Betray a faction and you'll spend multiple runs rebuilding trust. Different time horizons of reversibility.

### Persistence: Unlocks + Relationships
Faction relationships persist between runs (can degrade or improve). Faction-specific unlocks are earned through sustained alliance. Meta-progression is diplomatic history.

### Power Relationship: Dependent on Alignments
Power depends entirely on faction alignments. No personal growth outside factions. Your strength is borrowed strength.

### Element Interaction: Synergistic + Opposing
Certain faction combinations synergize (Fire and Forge create fire weapons). Others oppose (Shadow and Light cancel each other). Managing synergies and avoiding oppositions is the build challenge.

### Competition Type: Solo
Personal diplomacy. No multiplayer—the faction politics are between you and the game's factions.

### Progression Structure: Interconnected (Faction Web)
Factions are interconnected through alliances and enmities. Affecting one faction ripples through the web. The progression structure mirrors political complexity.

### Information Transparency: Partially Hidden (Faction Agendas)
You see faction standings (transparent). You don't see faction secret agendas (hidden). Factions may betray or reward you based on hidden criteria. Discovering agendas is part of progression.

### Feedback Loop: Delayed (Diplomatic Consequences)
Stance effects are immediate. But diplomatic choices have delayed consequences—a slight now might matter three runs later. The feedback timeline varies by choice type.

### Difficulty Arc: Variable (Faction Enemies)
Your enemies depend on your faction oppositions. Different diplomatic configurations create different enemy sets. You choose your difficulty by choosing your alignments.

### Completion State: Progress (Diplomatic Goals)
Each faction has long-term goals. Working toward any faction's goal is progress. "Victory" might be completing a faction's agenda arc over many runs.

### Randomness Role: Low (Deterministic Politics)
Faction behavior follows deterministic rules. Same actions produce same faction responses. The randomness is in dungeon encounters, not diplomatic systems. You can plan diplomacy precisely.

---

## Experimental Game 21: The Sculptor's Crucible

*A roguelite where you design your character's "shape" before each run, and that shape determines what abilities can fit—critical commitment to form before filling it with function.*

**Core Fantasy:** You're a soul sculptor. Before each run, you shape the vessel you'll inhabit—a spiritual body with specific dimensions and contours. Once shaped, you fill it with abilities that must fit. Broad vessels hold more but each ability is weaker. Narrow vessels hold less but each ability is stronger.

### Acquisition Source: Shape-Constrained
Abilities exist in the world, but you can only acquire ones that fit your shape. Shaped for fire? Fire abilities fit. Shaped narrow and deep? Only focused abilities fit. Your shape filters acquisition.

### Acquisition Timing: Frontloaded (Sculpting) + Distributed (Filling)
Sculpting is entirely pre-run. Filling the shape happens throughout the run as you find fitting abilities. The shape is frontloaded; the content is distributed.

### Resource Scarcity: Self-Imposed (Shape Limits)
Vessel capacity is fixed by your sculpting choices. Large shapes have more capacity but weaker abilities. Small shapes have less capacity but stronger abilities. You choose your scarcity through shape design.

### Resource Conversion: Invested (Shape Dimensions)
Shaping is investment. Each dimension you add expands capacity but dilutes power. You invest shape-space into specific dimensions.

### Choice Timing: Pre-Run (Sculpting) + Immediate (Filling)
Sculpting happens before departure with infinite time to design. Filling happens mid-run with immediate decisions about which fitting abilities to take.

**Pacing Subtable: Mixed**
Sculpting is untimed and deliberate. Filling follows run pacing—abilities appear and you decide quickly. Two modes, two paces.

### Commitment Weight: Critical (Shape)
**Subtable: Critical**
Once you begin the run, your shape is permanent. Every dimension, every contour, every capacity—locked. The most critical commitment in the game. Everything else follows from shape.

### Reversibility: Permanent (Shape) + Flexible (Contents)
Shape cannot change. But contents can be swapped if you find better-fitting abilities. You're permanently committed to the vessel, flexibly filling it.

### Persistence: Unlocks (Shape Templates)
Successful runs unlock shape templates—preset dimensions that worked. Also unlock new ability types that require specific shapes. Meta-progression expands sculpting vocabulary.

### Power Relationship: Dependent + Scaling
Power depends entirely on shape quality. But it also scales—well-filled shapes are stronger than poorly-filled identical shapes. Dependency on shape design, scaling within that design.

### Element Interaction: Spatial (Fit Interactions)
Abilities that fit adjacent shape regions interact. Synergies are spatial—abilities near each other in the shape combine. The sculpture's geography creates interaction patterns.

### Competition Type: Solo
Personal sculpting. No competition—artistic expression within game constraints.

### Progression Structure: Branching (Shape Trees)
Shape templates branch into families. Developing one shape family opens deeper shapes in that lineage. Your sculpting style branches based on what you practice.

### Information Transparency: Transparent (Shape Preview)
Before running, you see exactly what abilities could fit your shape. No hidden interactions. The challenge is designing shapes that attract the abilities you want.

### Feedback Loop: Immediate (Fit Feedback)
You immediately see when abilities fit or don't. Shape effectiveness is immediately apparent through gameplay. Feedback is continuous and clear.

### Difficulty Arc: Self-Determined (Shape Design)
Shape design determines difficulty. Safe shapes with many fitting abilities are easier. Ambitious narrow shapes with few fitting abilities are harder. You sculpt your difficulty.

### Completion State: Victory + Artistry
Complete the run with your sculpted vessel. But there's also artistry rating—how elegant was your shape? Mastery is winning with beautiful, efficient shapes.

### Randomness Role: Low (Deterministic Fitting)
Shape-ability fitting is deterministic. Same shape always accepts same abilities. Randomness is in which fitting abilities you encounter, not in what fits. Predictable system, variable encounters.

---

## Experimental Game 22: The Cascade

*A roguelite where choices generate new choices—each decision opens a "choice tree" that unfolds over time, and your build is the current state of many cascading decision trees.*

**Core Fantasy:** You're a chaos-wielder. Every choice you make spawns further choices. Pick a fire ability? It presents three fire modifications. Pick one modification? It presents two specializations. Your build is not a list of choices—it's the current state of many branching cascades.

### Acquisition Source: Choice-Generated
Choices aren't found in the world—they're generated by previous choices. The first choice is given. All subsequent choices are generated by the cascade. Your choices are the source of more choices.

### Acquisition Timing: Cascading
Each choice immediately generates follow-up choices. But those follow-ups can be deferred. You might have five pending cascades all wanting attention. Timing is about managing cascade resolution order.

### Resource Scarcity: Attention-Limited
Choices are abundant—cascades generate more than you can handle. The scarcity is attention. Each pending choice demands resolution. You can't pursue every cascade.

### Resource Conversion: Expanded
Choices aren't spent—they're expanded. One choice becomes three. Three become nine. The "currency" is cascade potential—how much unexplored choice-space you have.

### Choice Timing: Immediate + Deferred
New choices appear immediately when you make a choice. But you can defer them. Deferred choices remain pending, awaiting attention. You decide when to address each cascade.

**Pacing Subtable: Self-Paced with Accumulation**
You control when to make choices. But deferred choices accumulate. Eventually you must address cascades or drown in pending decisions. Self-paced within accumulation pressure.

### Commitment Weight: Low (Individual) + High (Cumulative)
**Subtable: Low individual, High cumulative**
Each choice is low commitment—many more follow. But the cumulative pattern of choices is high commitment. Your cascade trajectory is hard to redirect.

### Reversibility: Permanent (Cascade History)
Choices are permanent. But the system generates so many choices that mistakes are diluted. No single permanent choice matters much, but the permanent record matters completely.

### Persistence: Unlocks (Root Choices)
Meta-progression unlocks new "root choices"—the first choices that start cascades. Different roots create different cascade patterns. You're unlocking new chaos seeds.

### Power Relationship: Scaling (Cascade Depth)
Power scales with cascade depth. Deeper cascades (more follow-up choices resolved) create stronger abilities. Shallow wide cascades are weaker than deep narrow ones.

### Element Interaction: Emergent (Cascade Collisions)
When separate cascades reach compatible states, they can merge into super-cascades. The interaction is emergent—you can't fully predict what cascades will collide.

### Competition Type: Solo
Personal chaos management. No competition—just you versus the ever-expanding choice-space.

### Progression Structure: Interconnected (Cascade Web)
Cascades interconnect through collisions and shared decision points. The structure is a web, not a tree—choices in one cascade affect options in others.

### Information Transparency: Partially Hidden (Cascade Previews)
You see immediate next choices (transparent) but not where cascades eventually lead (hidden). Planning requires intuition about cascade trajectories.

### Feedback Loop: Cumulative (Cascade Results)
Individual choices give immediate feedback. But cascade patterns reveal themselves over time. The full feedback is cumulative—did your cascade strategy work?

### Difficulty Arc: Variable (Cascade Management)
Difficulty depends on how well you manage cascades. Overwhelming yourself with too many pending choices makes everything harder. Clean cascade management makes everything easier.

### Completion State: Progress (Cascade Mastery)
Runs complete when your cascades stabilize (no more pending choices) or when you die to accumulated chaos. Progress is learning to manage deeper cascades before stabilization.

### Randomness Role: Seeded (Cascade Patterns)
Cascades follow deterministic generation rules. Same choice at same cascade state generates same follow-ups. The system is seeded—learnable, but complex enough to feel random.

---

These 10 designs explore various combinations of the core ideas from your favorites:
- **Pre-run commitment** (Auction House, Gambler's, Score, Sculptor)
- **Tide/wave mechanics** (Wave Architect, Cascade)
- **Branching/navigation** (Bloodline, Cartographer)
- **Stance/loadout swapping** (Embassy, Toolkit)
- **Route/expedition planning** (Cartographer, Toolkit)

The most novel combinations are probably **The Score** (pre-composed builds that execute automatically), **The Cascade** (choices generating choices), and **The Sculptor** (shape commitment before content).

  6031→
